    <meta name="dc.description" content="Acclimatization is the last step of plants in vitro propagation while it comes to alter the environment conditions from tailor for plant requirements, sterile laboratory to external ex vitro conditions. Consequently, during acclimatization it may reach to plants mortality due to abiotic and biotic stresses occurring in external environment (high temperature, light intensity, low air relative humidity and the presence of microorganisms and pathogens in soil). Micropropagated plants develop alter organs on morphological, anatomical or biochemical levels which must be correct during acclimatization to improve adaptation of plants to ex vitro conditions. Therefore, there is a need to create acclimatization protocols to improve the effectiveness of this vegetative propagation method. So far there were formulated facilities as pre-acclimation, in vitro acclimatization, water cultures, CO2 enrichment, application of biostimulators and plant growth regulators. In following research we focused on describing previous achievements about the changes occurring in woody plants by micropropagation and summary of achievements in acclimatization of micropropagated woody plants. This article summary the current state of knowledge on acclimatization for various range of woody species by anatomical, physiological and biochemical levels. There are described ways to increase the survival of acclimatized plants and minimize acclimatization stress it also collects substances used so far to enhance plant growth during acclimatization. Acclimatization poses challenges in micropropagation of woody plants. During this stage, changes occur in plants. The ability of them to survey can be improved by various range of treatments."/>

    <meta property="og:url" content="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1"/>
    <meta property="og:type" content="article"/>
    <meta property="og:site_name" content="SpringerLink"/>
    <meta property="og:title" content="Challenges and insights in the acclimatization step of micropropagated woody plants - Plant Cell, Tissue and Organ Culture (PCTOC)"/>
    <meta property="og:description" content="Acclimatization is the last step of plants in vitro propagation while it comes to alter the environment conditions from tailor for plant requirements, sterile laboratory to external ex vitro conditions. Consequently, during acclimatization it may reach to plants mortality due to abiotic and biotic stresses occurring in external environment (high temperature, light intensity, low air relative humidity and the presence of microorganisms and pathogens in soil). Micropropagated plants develop alter organs on morphological, anatomical or biochemical levels which must be correct during acclimatization to improve adaptation of plants to ex vitro conditions. Therefore, there is a need to create acclimatization protocols to improve the effectiveness of this vegetative propagation method. So far there were formulated facilities as pre-acclimation, in vitro acclimatization, water cultures, CO2 enrichment, application of biostimulators and plant growth regulators. In following research we focused on describing previous achievements about the changes occurring in woody plants by micropropagation and summary of achievements in acclimatization of micropropagated woody plants. This article summary the current state of knowledge on acclimatization for various range of woody species by anatomical, physiological and biochemical levels. There are described ways to increase the survival of acclimatized plants and minimize acclimatization stress it also collects substances used so far to enhance plant growth during acclimatization."/>
    <meta property="og:image" content="https://static-content.springer.com/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs11240-024-02923-1/MediaObjects/11240_2024_2923_Fig1_HTML.png"/>

        <script class="js-entry">
    if (window.config.mustardcut) {
        (function(w, d) {
            
            
            
                window.Component = {};
                window.suppressShareButton = false;
                window.onArticlePage = true;
            

            var currentScript = d.currentScript || d.head.querySelector('script.js-entry');

            
            function catchNoModuleSupport() {
                var scriptEl = d.createElement('script');
                return (!('noModule' in scriptEl) && 'onbeforeload' in scriptEl)
            }

            var headScripts = [
                {'src': '/oscar-static/js/polyfill-es5-bundle-b4356fa7f5.js', 'async': false}
            ];

            var bodyScripts = [
                
                    
                    {'src': '/oscar-static/js/global-article-es5-bundle-a4d45088c4.js', 'async': false, 'module': false},
                    {'src': '/oscar-static/js/global-article-es6-bundle-951afb5c10.js', 'async': false, 'module': true}
                    
                
                
                    
                
                
                
            ];

            function createScript(script) {
                var scriptEl = d.createElement('script');
                scriptEl.src = script.src;
                scriptEl.async = script.async;
                if (script.module === true) {
                    scriptEl.type = "module";
                    if (catchNoModuleSupport()) {
                        scriptEl.src = '';
                    }
                } else if (script.module === false) {
                    scriptEl.setAttribute('nomodule', true)
                }
                if (script.charset) {
                    scriptEl.setAttribute('charset', script.charset);
                }

                return scriptEl;
            }

            for (var i = 0; i < headScripts.length; ++i) {
                var scriptEl = createScript(headScripts[i]);
                currentScript.parentNode.insertBefore(scriptEl, currentScript.nextSibling);
            }

            d.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
                for (var i = 0; i < bodyScripts.length; ++i) {
                    var scriptEl = createScript(bodyScripts[i]);
                    d.body.appendChild(scriptEl);
                }
            });

            // Webfont repeat view
            var config = w.config;
            if (config && config.publisherBrand && sessionStorage.fontsLoaded === 'true') {
                d.documentElement.className += ' webfonts-loaded';
            }
        })(window, document);
    }
</script>

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Challenges and insights in the acclimatization step of micropropagated woody plants","description":"Acclimatization is the last step of plants in vitro propagation while it comes to alter the environment conditions from tailor for plant requirements, sterile laboratory to external ex vitro conditions. Consequently, during acclimatization it may reach to plants mortality due to abiotic and biotic stresses occurring in external environment (high temperature, light intensity, low air relative humidity and the presence of microorganisms and pathogens in soil). Micropropagated plants develop alter organs on morphological, anatomical or biochemical levels which must be correct during acclimatization to improve adaptation of plants to ex vitro conditions. Therefore, there is a need to create acclimatization protocols to improve the effectiveness of this vegetative propagation method. So far there were formulated facilities as pre-acclimation, in vitro acclimatization, water cultures, CO2 enrichment, application of biostimulators and plant growth regulators. In following research we focused on describing previous achievements about the changes occurring in woody plants by micropropagation and summary of achievements in acclimatization of micropropagated woody plants. This article summary the current state of knowledge on acclimatization for various range of woody species by anatomical, physiological and biochemical levels. There are described ways to increase the survival of acclimatized plants and minimize acclimatization stress it also collects substances used so far to enhance plant growth during acclimatization. Acclimatization poses challenges in micropropagation of woody plants. During this stage, changes occur in plants.                 <div data-article-body="true" data-track-component="article body" class="c-article-body">

                    
                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Acclimatization is the last step of plants in vitro propagation while it comes to alter the environment conditions from tailor for plant requirements, sterile laboratory to external <i>ex vitro</i> conditions. Consequently, during acclimatization it may reach to plants mortality due to abiotic and biotic stresses occurring in external environment (high temperature, light intensity, low air relative humidity and the presence of microorganisms and pathogens in soil). Micropropagated plants develop alter organs on morphological, anatomical or biochemical levels which must be correct during acclimatization to improve adaptation of plants to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions. Therefore, there is a need to create acclimatization protocols to improve the effectiveness of this vegetative propagation method. So far there were formulated facilities as pre-acclimation, in vitro acclimatization, water cultures, CO<sub>2</sub> enrichment, application of biostimulators and plant growth regulators. In following research we focused on describing previous achievements about the changes occurring in woody plants by micropropagation and summary of achievements in acclimatization of micropropagated woody plants. This article summary the current state of knowledge on acclimatization for various range of woody species by anatomical, physiological and biochemical levels. There are described ways to increase the survival of acclimatized plants and minimize acclimatization stress it also collects substances used so far to enhance plant growth during acclimatization.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Abs2" data-title="Key message" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs2">Key message</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs2-content">
              
              <p>Acclimatization poses challenges in micropropagation of woody plants. During this stage, changes occur in plants. The ability of them to survey can be improved by various range of treatments.</p>
            </div></div></section>

                                <div class="main-content">
                                    <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Micropropagation allows to obtain high quality, disease free plants rapidly. The last step of this vegetative propagation method is acclimatization, defined as climatic or environmental plant adaptation (Hazarika et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hazarika BN, Teixeira da Silva JA, Talukdar A (2006) Effective acclimatization of in vitro cultured plants: methods, physiology and genetics. Floric Ornam Plant Biotechnol 2:428438" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e735">2006</a>). Acclimatization may result in significant mortality under the biotic and abiotic stresses present in external environment (high temperature, light intensity, low air relative humidity and the presence of microorganisms and pathogens in soil) (Chandra et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="Chandra S, Bandopadhyay R, Kumar V, Chandra R (2010) Acclimatization of tissue cultured plantlets: from laboratory to land. Biotechnol Lett 32:11991205" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e738">2010</a>; Kumar and Rao <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Kumar K, Rao IU (2012) Morphophysiological problems in acclimatization of micropropagated plants in ex vitro conditionsa review. J Ornam Hortic Plants 2(4):271283" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e741">2012</a>). This is the stage where in vitro plants are gradually exposed to normal environmental challenges, thus, are forced to develop complete survival mechanisms for a dynamic septic environment (Hiti-Bandaralage et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Hiti-Bandaralage JCA, Hayward A, Mitter N (2020) Structural relation for acclimatization success for in vitro cultured avocado. Acta Hortic 1285:269279. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2020.1285.39&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e744">2020</a>). Woody plants micropropagation and acclimatization, including nursery material requires to be developing, because overall woody plants do not grow in vitro well. This results from explanting season, age of the donor tree and type of primary explant. In woody plants, there are excessive phenolic exudations, basal callusing of shoot explants, shoot tip necrosis, and vitrification (Giri et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Giri CC, Shyamkumar B, Anjaneyulu C (2004) Progress in tissue culture, genetic transformation and applications of biotechnology to trees: an overview. Trees Struct Funct 18:115135. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00468-003-0287-6&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e747">2004</a>; Timofeeva et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2014" title="Timofeeva SN, Elkonin LA, Tyrnov VS (2014) Micropropagation of Laburnum anagyroides Medic. through axillary shoot regeneration. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 50:561567. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-014-9618-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR171" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e751">2014</a>). Therefore, in vitro propagation of woody plants is not very commonly practiced (Conde et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Conde P, Sousa A, Costa A, Santos CA (2007) Protocol for Ulmus minor Mill. micropropagation and acclimatization. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 92:113119" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e754">2007</a>; Ilczuk et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title='Ilczuk A, Jacygard E, Jagieo-Kubiec K, Pacholczak A (2013) Rozmananie in vitro rolin drzewiastych  perspektywy i problemy. Ogrod. ozdobne Sekt. Gospod. Nar. [in:] Ogrodnictwo ozdobne sektorem gospodarki narodowej, ed.&#34;J. Rabiza-wider, E. Skutnik, SGGW, Warszawa: 4148.' href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e757">2013</a>). However, there are successful micropropagation of species as <i>Salix tarraconensis</i> (Amo-Marco and Lledo <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="Amo-Marco JB, Lledo MD (1996) In vitro propagation of Salix tarraconensis Pau ex Font Quer, an endemic and threatened plant. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 32:4246" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e763">1996</a>) <i>Stereospermum chelonoides</i> (Shukla et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Shukla S, Shukla S, Mishra SK (2013) In vitro Regeneration of multipurpose medicinal tree stereospermum suaveolens factors controlling the in vitro regeneration. J Biotechnol Biomater 13(1). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.4172/2155-952X.S13-001&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR162" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e770">2013</a>), <i>Shorea robusta</i> (Singh et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2014" title="Singh M, Sonkusale S, Niratker C, Shukla P (2014) Micropropagation of Shorea robusta: an economically important woody plant. J For Sci 60(2): 7074. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17221/80/2013-JFS&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR166" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e776">2014</a>) <i>Rhododendron</i> (Pacholczak et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Pacholczak A, Winiarczyk A, Grzelak M, Nowakowska K (2020) Efficient in vitro propagation of rhododendron Ken Janeck. Propag Ornam Plants 20(3):8187" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR128" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e782">2020</a>) <i>Magnolia sirindhorniae</i> Noot. &amp; Chalermglin (Cui et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="Cui Y, Deng Y, Zheng K, Hu X, Zhu M, Deng X, Xi R (2019) An efficient micropropagation protocol for an endangered ornamental tree species (Magnolia sirindhorniae Noot. &amp; Chalermglin) and assessment of genetic uniformity through DNA markers. Sci Rep 9:9634. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-019-46050-w&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e789">2019</a>), <i>Citronella mucronata</i> (Guerra et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2022" title="Guerra F, Badilla L, Cautin R, Castro M (2022) Micropropagation of Citronella mucronata D. Don, a vulnerable chilean endemic tree species. Plants 11:2425. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/plants11182425&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e795">2022</a>), <i>Prunus ulmifolia</i> (Kirillov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Kirillov V, Pathak A, Patel SR, Serafimovich M, Daulenova M, Gorbachenkov M, Zholdasbayev M, Stikhareva T (2023) An efficient micropropagation protocol for an endangered tree species Aflatunia ulmifolia (Franch.) Vassilcz. In Vitro Cell Dev Biol -Plant 60:2838. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-023-10392-y&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e801">2023</a>). Propagation of herbaceous plants is not extremely challenging by extension more commonly used. It is due to unreliable flowering habit and quick loss of viability as well as low seed germination rate and slow growth. Moreover, conventional way of propagation is more time-consuming and do not yield virus-free planting material (Lebedev et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Lebedev V, Arkaev M, Dremova M, Pozdniakov I, Shestibratov K (2018) Effects of growth regulators and gelling agents on ex vitro rooting of raspberry. Plants 8(1):3. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/plants8010003&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e804">2018</a>). In glass plants have assured stable conditions to grow consequent on availability of nutrients, high humidity, the gaseous environment and the composition of medium. Additionally, microplants are placed in growing rooms where the quality, quantity of light and the temperature is adjusted to plants (Pincelli-Souza et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Pincelli-Souza RP, Tillmann M, Esler M, Alves CCD, Cohen JD (2018) Hybrid hazelnut: micropropagation, rooting and acclimatization. Acta Hortic 1191:113120. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2018.1191.16&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR134" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e808">2018</a>). The sudden change in growth conditions contributes to significant stress and can result in a substantial reduction in the efficiency of this propagation method. Consequently, plants are induced to develop survival mechanisms in the variable and challenging external environment. The techniques using during the acclimatization stage require lower relative humidity, higher light intensity, stimulation of autotrophic growth in plants, and the characteristic septic environmental conditions typical of greenhouse or field settings. In comparison to the micropropagation of herbaceous plants, in vitro propagation of woody plants poses a greater difficulty. In recent years, efforts have been made to improve large-scale micropropagation techniques for woody plants. However, many species within this group still encounter issues with micropropagation protocols, which involve determining the appropriate growth conditions, such as growth regulator application and nutrient medium (Rathore et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Rathore JS, Rathore V, Shekhawat NS, Singh RP, Liler G, Phulwaria M, Dagla HR (2004) Micropropagation of woody plants. Plant Biotechnol Molec Markers, pp 195205. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/1-4020-3213-7_13&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR147" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e811">2004</a>; Jain and Hggman <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Jain SM, Hggman H (2007) Protocols for micropropagation of woody trees and fruits. Protoc Micropropag Woody Trees Fruits, pp 1559. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/978-1-4020-6352-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e814">2007</a>; Gaidamashvili and Benelli <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Gaidamashvili M, Benelli C (2021) Threatened woody plants of georgia and micropropagation as a tool for in vitro conservation. Agronomy 11(6):120. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11061082&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e817">2021</a>). Inducing root formation in this group of woody plants is also a challenge in micropropagation (Ak <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Ak BE (2018) The importance of in vitro micropropagation of fruit crops. In: First international GAP agriculture and livestock congress proceedings book. (ISBN 978-975-7113-65-2):716723." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e820">2018</a>). In woody plants, anatomical changes in stems, leaves, and roots that occur during growth in the laboratory can affect plant processes such as photosynthesis, transpiration, and mineral nutrient uptake (Rohr et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Rohr R, Iliev I, Scaltsoyinnes A, Tsoulpha P (2003) Acclimatization of micropropagated forest trees. Acta Hortic 616:5969. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2003.616.3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR153" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e823">2003</a>). Hiti-Bandaralage et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Hiti-Bandaralage JCA, Hayward A, OBrien C., Beveridge C, Mitter N (2018) Acclimatization of micropropagated mature avocado. Acta Hortic. 1224:1320. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2018.1224.3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e827">2018</a>) suggests that even if the explant is rooted, surviving the acclimatization process is demanding due to the small number of unbranched adventitious roots produced during the rooting stage. Environmental changes lead to oxidative stress, resulting in disruptions in plant development and potentially leading to plant death (Sharma et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Sharma P, Jha AB, Dubey RS, Pessarakli M (2012) Reactive oxygen species, oxidative damage, and antioxidative defense mechanism in plants under stressful conditions. J Bot. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1155/2012/217037&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR158" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e830">2012</a>). So far, most of the research has been dedicated to improving the efficiency of the in vitro micropropagation process itself, with less literature focusing on optimizing the acclimatization process (Hazarika et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hazarika BN, Teixeira da Silva JA, Talukdar A (2006) Effective acclimatization of in vitro cultured plants: methods, physiology and genetics. Floric Ornam Plant Biotechnol 2:428438" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e833">2006</a>). To increase the scale of woody plant propagation under laboratory conditions, it is necessary to refine existing protocols and develop new propagation protocols.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Differences in plants growing in vitro and in external conditions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Differences in plants growing in vitro and in external conditions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><p>Plants grown in laboratory or field can differ from each other at morphological, anatomical, physiological, biochemical, and molecular levels. The conditions during the regeneration of explants in the laboratory are specific. Micropropagated plants grow in tightly closed vessels, preventing the entry of harmful microorganisms but limiting the supply of CO<sub>2</sub> and the release of gases produced by the plants. Additionally, these plants are provided with high relative humidity, low light intensity, a source of energy in the form of sugars, and growth regulators (Pospsilov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1999" title="Pospsilov J, Ticha I, Kadlecek P, Haisel D, Plzakova S (1999) Acclimatization of micropropagated plants to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 42:481497. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1002688208758&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e846">1999</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Anatomical and physiological differences and abnormalities in micropropagated and acclimated woody plants</h3><p>The main problem in plant acclimatization is the loss of plant turgor and necrotic changes that occur due to moisture loss when transferred to external conditions (Pospsilov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1999" title="Pospsilov J, Ticha I, Kadlecek P, Haisel D, Plzakova S (1999) Acclimatization of micropropagated plants to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 42:481497. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1002688208758&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e856">1999</a>). Anatomical abnormalities caused by in vitro propagation (in leaves, stems, and roots) can negatively impact processes as photosynthesis, transpiration, and the uptake of mineral nutrients and water (Rohr et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Rohr R, Iliev I, Scaltsoyinnes A, Tsoulpha P (2003) Acclimatization of micropropagated forest trees. Acta Hortic 616:5969. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2003.616.3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR153" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e859">2003</a>). In vitro plants have a low layer of waxes and thin epidermis. Acclimatization issues also arise from the physiological characteristics of regenerated plant leaves, which have a reduced ability to undergo photosynthesis due to improper stomatal functioning, resulting in significant water loss and irreversible dehydration. Most micropropagated plants lack the development of a root hair zone (Pospsilov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1999" title="Pospsilov J, Ticha I, Kadlecek P, Haisel D, Plzakova S (1999) Acclimatization of micropropagated plants to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 42:481497. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1002688208758&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e862">1999</a>; Hazarika et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hazarika BN, Teixeira da Silva JA, Talukdar A (2006) Effective acclimatization of in vitro cultured plants: methods, physiology and genetics. Floric Ornam Plant Biotechnol 2:428438" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e865">2006</a>; Erst et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Erst A, Novikova TI, Karkulov A, Zaytseva Y (2012) Adaptation of regenerants Rhododendron hybridum to ex vitro conditions. Sci Bull BSU 9 (128: 8). Belgorod State Univ., Belgorod." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e868">2012</a>). Due to the favorable conditions in laboratory, they develop disrupted organs, leading to disorders such as vitrification, improper stomatal functioning, abnormal growth and development, and a loss of photosynthetic capacity (Hazarika et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hazarika BN, Teixeira da Silva JA, Talukdar A (2006) Effective acclimatization of in vitro cultured plants: methods, physiology and genetics. Floric Ornam Plant Biotechnol 2:428438" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e872">2006</a>; Kumar and Rao <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Kumar K, Rao IU (2012) Morphophysiological problems in acclimatization of micropropagated plants in ex vitro conditionsa review. J Ornam Hortic Plants 2(4):271283" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e875">2012</a>; Tisarum et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Tisarum R, Samphumphung T, Theerawitaya C, Prommee W, Cha-um S (2018) In vitro photoautotrophic acclimatization, direct transplantation and ex vitro adaptation of rubber tree (Hevea brasiliensis). Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 133:215223. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-017-1374-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR172" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e878">2018</a>). Plants in laboratory are photosynthetically inactive, with poorly lignified tissues, slightly thickened cells, large intercellular spaces and weakly developed vascular system (Ldo et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Ldo A, Pereira Gomes KK, Barboza BSC, Serra Seca Vieira G, Almeida Tupinamb E, Menezes de Arago W (2007) Cultivo in vitro de embries zigticos e aclimatao de plntulas de coqueiro-ano. Pesqui Agropecuria Bras 42(2):147154. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0100-204X2007000200002&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e881">2007</a>; de Oliveira et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="de Oliveira LM, Paiva R, de Santana JRF, Alves E, Nogueira C, Dionsio F (2008) Effect of cytokinins on in vitro development of autotrophism and acclimatization of Annona glabra L. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 44:128135. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-008-9119-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e884">2008</a>; Sa et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Sa FP, da Silva LA, Espindola Amorim JAE, Cruz da Silva AV, Pasqual M (2016) In vitro propagation and acclimatization of genipapo accessions. Cincia e Agrotecnol 40:155163. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/1413-70542016402036015&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR155" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e887">2016</a>). In physiological terms, rapid water loss leading to low plant survival rates is attributed to two main factors: high cuticular transpiration rates due to underdeveloped epicuticular waxes and a lack of control in the functioning of stomata (Santamaria et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1993" title="Santamaria JM, Davies W, Atkinson CJ (1993) Stomata of micropropagated Delphinium plants respond to ABA, CO2, light and water potential, but fail to close fully. J Exp Bot 44:99107. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/jxb/44.1.99&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR156" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e891">1993</a>; Bandyopadhyay et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Bandyopadhyay T, Gangopadhyay G, Poddar R, Mukherjee KK (2004) Trichomes: their diversity, distribution and density in acclimatization of teak (Tectona grandis L.) Plants Grown in vitro. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 78:113121. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/B:TICU.0000022534.03276.c5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e894">2004</a>). In glass, plants generally produce many of large, often fully open stomata due to nearly 100% relative humidity in the vessel (Radenbaugh and Ruzin 1989). They also exhibit an abnormal shape and structure. Stomatal cells have thinner walls and contain higher levels of starch and chloroplasts (Marin et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1988" title="Marin JA, Gella R, Herrero M (1988) Stomatal structure and functioning as a response to environmental changes in acclimatozed micropropagated Prunus cerasus L. Ann Bot 62:663670" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR111" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e897">1988</a>). The exudates often produce small amounts of epicuticular waxes and cuticles, with many stomatas that additionally function improperly. Consequently, during the acclimatization stage, there is excessive and uncontrolled transpiration. No and Bonini (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="No N, Bonini L (1996) Leaf anatomy of highbush blueberry grown in vitro and during acclimatization to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 38(1):1925. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF02879626&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR121" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e900">1996</a>) demonstrated that <i>Vaccinium corymbosum</i> plants grown in vitro lost 50% of their water within 2.5h compared to field-grown plants (24%) (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Tab1">1</a>). Sharma et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Sharma U, Kataria V, Shekhawat NS (2017) In vitro propagation, ex vitro rooting and leaf micromorphology of Bauhinia racemosa Lam.: a leguminous tree with medicinal values. Physiol Mol Biol Plants 23:969977. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s12298-017-0459-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR159" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e910">2017</a>) <i>Bauhinia racemosa</i> L. noted several differences between glass-cultured plants and acclimatized plants. The vein density in plants grown in vitro was lower than in acclimatized plants, glass-cultured plants had fewer trichomes, and the stomata in vitro were densely distributed and malfunctioned as they remained open, whereas acclimatized plants had properly functioning stomata, presented in lower numbers. The authors shows the gradual acclimatization of plants which is a prerequisite for survival and successful establishment in field conditions. The repair process of anatomy is crucial to proper growth and development of plants. Shekhawat et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Shekhawat MS, Manokari M, Revathi J (2017) In vitro propagation and ex vitro rooting of Aerva lanata (L.) Juss. ex Schult.: a rare medicinal plant. Indian J Plant Physiol 22:4047. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40502-016-0248-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR160" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e916">2021</a>) reports that leaves of 4weeks old greenhouse hardened of the tree <i>Santalum album</i> L. plantlets for 4weeks. The malfunctioning and structure of stomata lead to insufficient photosynthetic capacity to achieve a positive carbon balance. The density and distribution of trichomes are important for maintaining a high relative water content, while fully formed veins serve the transport of water and carbohydrates and provide mechanical leaf strength (Roth-Nebelsick et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2001" title="Roth-Nebelsick A, Uhl D, Mosbrugger V, Kerp H (2001) Evolution and function of leaf venation architecture: a review. Ann Bot 87:553566. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1006/anbo.2001.1391&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR154" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e922">2001</a>; Bandyopadhyay et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Bandyopadhyay T, Gangopadhyay G, Poddar R, Mukherjee KK (2004) Trichomes: their diversity, distribution and density in acclimatization of teak (Tectona grandis L.) Plants Grown in vitro. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 78:113121. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/B:TICU.0000022534.03276.c5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e925">2004</a>). Weaker trichome distribution in <i>Tectona grandis</i> L. leaves in vitro, compared to <i>ex vitro</i>, correlated with water loss, leading to a low plant survival rate after transplantation (Bandyopadhyay et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Bandyopadhyay T, Gangopadhyay G, Poddar R, Mukherjee KK (2004) Trichomes: their diversity, distribution and density in acclimatization of teak (Tectona grandis L.) Plants Grown in vitro. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 78:113121. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/B:TICU.0000022534.03276.c5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e935">2004</a>). For explants to acclimate to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions, physiological and anatomical adaptations must take place (Ldo et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Ldo A, Pereira Gomes KK, Barboza BSC, Serra Seca Vieira G, Almeida Tupinamb E, Menezes de Arago W (2007) Cultivo in vitro de embries zigticos e aclimatao de plntulas de coqueiro-ano. Pesqui Agropecuria Bras 42(2):147154. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0100-204X2007000200002&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e941">2007</a>; Sa et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Sa FP, da Silva LA, Espindola Amorim JAE, Cruz da Silva AV, Pasqual M (2016) In vitro propagation and acclimatization of genipapo accessions. Cincia e Agrotecnol 40:155163. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/1413-70542016402036015&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR155" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e944">2016</a>). There is the spongy parenchyma with irregular structure and a small amount of palisade mesophyll. Lack of differentiation into both forms can also occur. Observations of avocado stomata showed that they changed their shape and size within a month (Hiti-Bandaralage et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Hiti-Bandaralage JCA, Hayward A, Mitter N (2020) Structural relation for acclimatization success for in vitro cultured avocado. Acta Hortic 1285:269279. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2020.1285.39&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e948">2020</a>). No and Bonini, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="No N, Bonini L (1996) Leaf anatomy of highbush blueberry grown in vitro and during acclimatization to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 38(1):1925. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF02879626&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR121" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e951">1996</a>) demonstrated in <i>Vaccinium corymbosum</i> that leaves cultured in vitro had a greater number of smaller stomata (361 per mm<sup>2</sup>) with ring-shaped stomatal cells. In contrast, plants grown under field conditions had 241 per mm<sup>2</sup> stomata with elliptical stomatal cells. Anatomical analyses of <i>Vaccinium corymbosum</i> leaves cultured in vitro revealed small, round cells with discontinuous and disorganized spongy mesophyll and numerous intercellular spaces, with a palisade-to-spongy mesophyll ratio of 1:1.5. Leaves of blueberry seedlings showed significant anatomical differences until 6 months after removal from glass culture, at which point they exhibited anatomical features similar to field-grown plants, including rectangular palisade mesophyll cells, spongy mesophyll with 34 layers, and intercellular spaces surrounding stomata. Our initial studies on <i>Rhododendron</i> seem to show that in vitro plants leaves develop irregular parenchyma, not differentiated into spongy and palisade (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Fig1">1</a>a, b). It is mentioned that the narrow cuticle development, epicuticular waxes deposition and functional stomata during in vitro culture causes uninhibited transpiration rates in leaves of plantlets taken out of the culture vessels (Chirina et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Chirina CF, Pasqual M, de Araujo AG, Pereira AR, Castro EM (2012) Acclimatization and leaf anatomy of micropropagated fig plantlets. Rev Bras Frutic 34(4):11801188. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0100-29452012000400027&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e971">2012</a>). This increase in thickness, observed along acclimatization, is useful in avoiding the excessive loss of water, which avoids desiccation of plantlets when transferred to a field environment (Casson and Gray <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Casson S, Gray JE (2008) Influence environmental factors on stomatal development. New Phytol Cambridge 178:923. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1469-8137.2007.02351.x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e974">2008</a>). The studies of Chirina et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Chirina CF, Pasqual M, de Araujo AG, Pereira AR, Castro EM (2012) Acclimatization and leaf anatomy of micropropagated fig plantlets. Rev Bras Frutic 34(4):11801188. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0100-29452012000400027&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e977">2012</a>) in fig plantlets revealed the increase in waxes thickness, observed along acclimatization as useful in avoiding the excessive loss of water, which avoids desiccation of plantlets when transferred to a field environment. Our research seem to confirm the previous research (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Fig1">1</a>c, d). During the initial period of acclimatization, there is also a disturbance in the photosynthesis process (Hazarika et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hadi-Takovi V, ukalovi V, Vuleti M (2007) The relationship between respiration rate and peroxidase activities in maize root mitochondria. Biol Plant 51:297302. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-007-0059-z&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e984">2006</a>). In vitro growing plants stem anatomy is also altered in comparison to acclimatized. Chlorenchyma in in vitro growing plants was absent while in 12week old acclimatized plants consisted of 68 layers. Sclerenchymatous fibres only at acclimatized plants were well developed. As well as vascular bundles and medullary ray development. The secondary xylem and phloem differentiation was detected and the center portion was occupied by thin-walled and reduced parenchymatous pith (Shekhawat et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Shekhawat MS, Manokari M, Revathi J (2017) In vitro propagation and ex vitro rooting of Aerva lanata (L.) Juss. ex Schult.: a rare medicinal plant. Indian J Plant Physiol 22:4047. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40502-016-0248-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR160" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e987">2021</a>). In glass culture, plants, which receive energy directly from the nutrient solution, are not inclined towards heterotrophy. It is only after removal from the glass culture and during acclimatization that they become fully autotrophic. This is evident in the results obtained by Faisal and Anis, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Faisal M, Anis M (2009) Changes in photosynthetic activity, pigment composition, electrolyte leakage, lipid peroxidation, and antioxidant enzymes during ex vitro establishment of micropropagated Rauvolfia tetraphylla plantlets. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 99:125132. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-009-9584-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e990">2009</a>), where the photosynthetic rate increased from nearly 0 to 2.03.0mol CO<sub>2</sub> m<sup>2</sup>s<sup>1</sup> within 28days, regardless of treatment. Similarly, Jagieo-Kubiec et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021b" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, ukaszewska AJ, Pacholczak A (2021b) Acclimation to ex vitro conditions in ninebark. Agronomy 11(4):612. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11040612&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1000">2021b</a>) observed an increase in the photosynthetic rate during the acclimatization of bladderwort plants. Different gas exchange parameters are also observed in glass culture and during acclimation. Then, the photosynthesis rate increases, while transpiration and stomatal conductance decrease (Jagieo-Kubiec et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021b" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, ukaszewska AJ, Pacholczak A (2021b) Acclimation to ex vitro conditions in ninebark. Agronomy 11(4):612. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11040612&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1003">2021b</a>). Plant roots grown in vitro have low water conductivity and weak root-stem connections, making water uptake challenging. Therefore, the structure of leaves and roots developed under laboratory conditions significantly influences the success of the acclimatization stage (Pospsilov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1999" title="Pospsilov J, Ticha I, Kadlecek P, Haisel D, Plzakova S (1999) Acclimatization of micropropagated plants to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 42:481497. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1002688208758&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1006">1999</a>; Hiti-Bandaralage et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Hiti-Bandaralage JCA, Hayward A, OBrien C., Beveridge C, Mitter N (2018) Acclimatization of micropropagated mature avocado. Acta Hortic. 1224:1320. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2018.1224.3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1009">2018</a>). urkovi et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="urkovi J, Lengyelov A, aov I, Kurjak D, Hladk D (2009) Photosynthetic performance and stomatal characteristics during ex vitro acclimatisation of true service tree (Sorbus domestica L.). J Hortic Sci Biotechnol 84(2):223227. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/14620316.2009.11512508&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1012">2009</a>) suggest that the shedding of leaves produced in the growth chamber and their rapid replacement with those acclimated to the new conditions may be one of the strategies plants use to adapt (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Fig2">2</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table1 The list of woody species with changes or abnormalities occurring in the acclimatization period on anatomical and physiological level</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs11240-024-02923-1/MediaObjects/11240_2024_2923_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig2" height="386"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>Scheme of abnormalities in in vitro growing plants on morphological, anatomical, physiological and biochemical response of plants during acclimatization</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">The biochemical response of plants to acclimatization</h3><p>The substantial difference in vapor pressure between in vitro and <i>ex vitro</i> can induce water stress in acclimatized plants. Stress can lead to an imbalance between light energy absorption and utilization, resulting in oxidative stress and consequently an increase in the content of reactive oxygen species (ROS) [e.g. hydrogen peroxide (H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>), superoxide radicals (O<sup>2</sup>), singlet oxygen (O<sup>2</sup>), hydroxyl radicals (HO<sup></sup>)] (Ali et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2005" title="Ali MB, Hahn EJ, Paek KY (2005) Effects of light intensities on antioxidant enzymes and malondialdehyde content during short-term acclimatization on micropropagated Phalaenopsis plantlet. Environ Exp Bot 54(2):109120. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.envexpbot.2004.06.005&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1564">2005</a>; Bakov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Bakov P, Pospilov J, Synkov H (2008) Production of reactive oxygen species and development of antioxidative systems during in vitro growth and ex vitro transfer. Biol Plant 52:413422. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-008-0085-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1567">2008</a>; Faisal and Anis <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Faisal M, Anis M (2009) Changes in photosynthetic activity, pigment composition, electrolyte leakage, lipid peroxidation, and antioxidant enzymes during ex vitro establishment of micropropagated Rauvolfia tetraphylla plantlets. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 99:125132. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-009-9584-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1570">2009</a>; Dias et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Dias MC, Pinto G, Santos C (2011) Acclimatization of micropropagated plantlets induces an antioxidative burst: a case study with Ulmus minor Mill. Photosynthetica 49:259266. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11099-011-0028-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1573">2011</a>). As a result of oxidative stress, there may also be an increase in malondialdehyde (MDA) content. Excessive accumulation of ROS leads to lipid peroxidation and, consequently, membrane damage, protein degradation, enzyme inactivation, and DNA damage (Hernndez et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hernndez JA, Escobar C, Creissen G, Mullineaux PM (2006) Antioxidant enzyme induction in pea plants under high irradiance. Biol Plant 50:395399" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1576">2006</a>; Hadi-Takovi et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Hadi-Takovi V, ukalovi V, Vuleti M (2007) The relationship between respiration rate and peroxidase activities in maize root mitochondria. Biol Plant 51:297302. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-007-0059-z&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1580">2007</a>; Bakov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Bakov P, Pospilov J, Synkov H (2008) Production of reactive oxygen species and development of antioxidative systems during in vitro growth and ex vitro transfer. Biol Plant 52:413422. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-008-0085-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1583">2008</a>). The antioxidant system is reported to be fimportant in determining the ability of plants to survive oxidative which include low molecular mass antioxidants (ascorbate, carotenoids, glutathione, tocopherols, phenols) as well as several antioxidative enzymes [ascorbate peroxidase (APX), catalase, (CAT), glutathione reductase (GR), monodehydroascorbate reductase (MDHAR), dehydroascorbate reductase (DHAR), superoxide dismutase (SOD) (Faisal and Anis <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Faisal M, Anis M (2009) Changes in photosynthetic activity, pigment composition, electrolyte leakage, lipid peroxidation, and antioxidant enzymes during ex vitro establishment of micropropagated Rauvolfia tetraphylla plantlets. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 99:125132. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-009-9584-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1586">2009</a>; Hernndez et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Hernndez JA, Escobar C, Creissen G, Mullineaux PM (2006) Antioxidant enzyme induction in pea plants under high irradiance. Biol Plant 50:395399" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1589">2006</a>; Zlatev et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Zlatev ZS, Lidon FC, Ramalho JC, Yordanov IT (2006) Comparison of resistance to drought of three bean cultivars. Biol Plant 50:389439. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-006-0054-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR189" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1592">2006</a>; Bakov et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Bakov P, Pospilov J, Synkov H (2008) Production of reactive oxygen species and development of antioxidative systems during in vitro growth and ex vitro transfer. Biol Plant 52:413422. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-008-0085-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1595">2008</a>). The acclimatized <i>Ulmus minor</i> showed increased levels of MDA and electrolyte leakage, indicating oxidative stress (Dias et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Dias MC, Pinto G, Santos C (2011) Acclimatization of micropropagated plantlets induces an antioxidative burst: a case study with Ulmus minor Mill. Photosynthetica 49:259266. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11099-011-0028-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1602">2011</a>). Earlier research of Faisal and Anis (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Faisal M, Anis M (2009) Changes in photosynthetic activity, pigment composition, electrolyte leakage, lipid peroxidation, and antioxidant enzymes during ex vitro establishment of micropropagated Rauvolfia tetraphylla plantlets. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 99:125132. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-009-9584-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1605">2009</a>) reported that at the beginning of acclimatization, there was an increase in electrolyte leakage, TBARS content, SOD and GR activity. A gradual increase in CAT and APX activity were observed as well. They also emphasized that plants exhibit the ability to develop an enzymatic antioxidant defense system to survive oxidative stress and reduce the release of free radicals. Moreover, the levels of chl a, chl b and carotenoids (Cx+c) increased. Quantitatively, ROS accumulation was detected in <i>Vitis vinifera</i>. It was found that O<sup>2</sup> was uniformly distributed, while H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> accumulated preferentially in veins, wounds, stomatal guards, and surrounding cells. They also noted a correlation between the presence of H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and the degree of stomatas (Vilela et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Vilela BJ, Carvalho LC, Ferreira J, Amncio S (2007) Gain of function of stomatal movements in rooting Vitis vinifera L. plants: regulation by H2O2 is independent of ABA before the protruding of roots. Plant Cell Rep 26:21492157. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00299-007-0427-3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR175" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1622">2007</a>). Another indicator of stress reactions occurring in plants may be an increased level of free proline. Proline is considered the primary accumulated metabolite in various stress conditions, helping to maintain water absorption capacity and improve drought tolerance for plant survival and establishment (Kishor et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1995" title="Kishor PK, Hong Z, Miao GH, Hu CAA (1995) Overexpression of [delta]-pyrroline-5-carboxylate synthetase increases proline production and confers osmotolerance in transgenic plants. Plant Physiol 108(4):13871394. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1104/pp.108.4.1387&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1625">1995</a>; Molinari et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Molinari HBC, Marur CJ, Daros E, De Campos MKF, Pereira LFP (2007) Evaluation of the stress-inducible production of proline in transgenic sugarcane (Saccharum spp.): osmotic adjustment, chlorophyll fluorescence and oxidative stress. Physiol Plant 130:218229. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1399-3054.2007.00909.x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1628">2007</a>; Liang et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Liang X, Zhang L, Natarajan SK (2013) Proline mechanisms of stress survival. Antioxid Redox Signal&#xA; 19:9981011. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1089/ars.2012.5074&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1632">2013</a>). It was found that proline could serve as an indicator of plant stress levels after <i>ex vitro</i> transfer, with its rapid accumulation indicating severe water stress during acclimatization. High levels of free proline were observed, in acclimatized mulberry plants (Huh et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Huh YS, Lee JK, Nam SY (2017) Improvement of ex vitro acclimatization of mulberry plantlets by supplement of abscisic acid to the last subculture medium. J Plant Biotechnol 44:431437. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.5010/JPB.2017.44.4.431&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1638">2017</a>) (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Tab2">2</a>). The increased chl content can improve the antioxidant capabilities of plants against abiotic stresses (Barickman et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2014" title="Barickman TC, Kopsell DA, Sams CE (2014) Abscisic acid increases carotenoid and chlorophyll concentrations in leaves and fruit of two tomato genotypes. J Am Soc Hortic Sci 139(3):261266. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/jashs.139.3.261&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1644">2014</a>; Huh et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Huh YS, Lee JK, Nam SY (2017) Improvement of ex vitro acclimatization of mulberry plantlets by supplement of abscisic acid to the last subculture medium. J Plant Biotechnol 44:431437. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.5010/JPB.2017.44.4.431&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1647">2017</a>). Shekhawat et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Shekhawat MS, Manokari M, Revathi J (2017) In vitro propagation and ex vitro rooting of Aerva lanata (L.) Juss. ex Schult.: a rare medicinal plant. Indian J Plant Physiol 22:4047. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40502-016-0248-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR160" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1651">2021</a>) on Indian sandalwood proved that photosynthetic pigments chlorophyll a, chl b, chl a+b (339.00.23 initially, 585.00.20 in the hardened plants) and carotenoids (56.00.22 in vitro and 75.00.13 in acclimatized plants) level significantly increases in acclimatization period.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table2 The list of species where biochemical changes in the acclimatization period occurred</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1/tables/2" aria-label="Full size table 2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section data-title="The effect of plant genotype to acclimatization"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec5-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec5">The effect of plant genotype to acclimatization</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec5-content"><p>Plant genotype can also affect acclimatization. For example, <i>Bougainvillea</i> 'Mahatma Gandi' achieved a 74% acclimatization rate, whereas the 'Refulgens' variety survived at a rate of 38.12% under the same conditions. It was observed that significantly higher survival rates were seen in plants grown in glass jars covered with polypropylene film (Pratiksha et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Pratiksha K, Kishan S, Janakiram T, Singh SK, Prasad KV, Ritu J (2016) In vitro sterilization, rooting and acclimatization of difficult-to-root Bougainvillea Cultivars. Int J Bio-Resour Stress Manage 7(3):412419" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR142" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1844">2016</a>). Reed, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1995" title="Reed BM (1995) Screening Pyrus germplasm for in vitro rooting response. HortScience 30:12921294. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTSCI.30.6.1292&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR151" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1847">1995</a>) suggests that pear, which acclimatize with difficulty due to various genetic responses, should have their container lids opened 2days before <i>ex vitro</i> transfer to allow better airflow. Subsequently, the plants are placed in a light potting mix and covered with a transparent lid to ensure high humidity around the plants. The ability to acclimatize has also been observed to be genotype-dependent in <i>Juglans regia</i>. The 'MB-T-231' variety achieved a 25% acclimatization rate, while 'Serr' reached 83%. The influence of genotype on acclimatization has been demonstrated (Dolcet-Sanjuan et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="Dolcet-Sanjuan R, Claveria E, Camprub A, Estan V, Calvet C (1996) Micropropagation of walnut trees (Juglans regia L.) and response to arbuscular mycorrhizal inoculation. Agronomie 16:639645. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1051/agro:19961008&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1857">1996</a>). Avocado acclimatization of the 'Velvick' variety presented a much greater challenge than the 'Reed' variety, with survival rates of 40 and 97%, respectively. A dominant fascicular cambium and less phloem fibres in stems correlated with the enhanced rooting. Acclimatization success positively correlated to the presence of fully differentiated secondary xylem in roots. The smaller epidermal cells, high stomatal density and reduced vein termination density was correlated with reduced acclimation success (Hiti-Bandaralage et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2022" title="Hiti-Bandaralage J, Hayward A, Mitter N (2022) Structural Disparity of avocado rootstocks in vitro for rooting and acclimation success. Int J Plant Biol 13(4):426442. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/ijpb13040035&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1860">2022</a>).</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Ways to increase the survival of acclimatized woody plants and minimize acclimatization stress"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec6-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec6">Ways to increase the survival of acclimatized woody plants and minimize acclimatization stress</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec6-content"><p>Murashige, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1974" title="Murashige T (1974) Plant propagation through tissue culture. Ann Rev Plant Physiol 25:135166. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1146/annurev.pp.25.060174.001031&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR120" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1871">1974</a>) suggested two strategies that can ensure success in woody plants acclimatization. The first involves stimulating micropropagated plantlets to become autotrophic, the second is reducing water stress by changing the culture environment (Rohr et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Rohr R, Iliev I, Scaltsoyinnes A, Tsoulpha P (2003) Acclimatization of micropropagated forest trees. Acta Hortic 616:5969. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2003.616.3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR153" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1874">2003</a>). To improve the efficiency of acclimatizing woody plants, both in vitro and during transfer to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions, various treatments, preparations, and substances are used, such as growth regulators, biostimulators, antitranspirants (Clapa et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Clapa D, Fira A, Joshee N (2013) An efficient ex vitro rooting and acclimatization method for horticultural plants using float hydroculture.
