HortScience 48(9):11591167. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/hortsci.48.9.1159&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1880">2013</a>; Dimitrova and Berova <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Dimitrova N, Berova M (2020) Optimisation of rooting and acclimatization of Pyrus communis L. with the biostimulator Charkor. Silva Balcanica 20(3):4756" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1883">2020</a>). The period of acclimatization is also important because high temperatures in the summer can reduce plant survival. A commonly used method for acclimatizing in vitro propagated plantlets is the use of a weaning chamber with a scheduled misting system to maintain humidity (Yahy et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2015" title="Xia XJ, Fang PP, Guo X, Qian X, Zhou J, Shi K, Zhou YH, Yu JQ (2018) Brassinosteroid-mediated apoplastic H2O2glutaredoxin 12/14 cascade regulates antioxidant capacity in response to chilling in tomato. Plant Cell Environ 41(5):10521064. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/pce.13052&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR179" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1887">2015</a>). To mitigate plant responses to <i>ex vitro</i> transfer, plants should be gradually acclimated to the new, less favorable conditions. This includes reducing relative humidity and increasing the CO<sub>2</sub> concentration (Kanuchova and urkovi <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Kanuchova A, urkovi J (2013) Wood ontogeny during ex vitro acclimatization in micropropagated hybrid poplar clones. Biol Plant 57:144148. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10535-012-0122-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1895">2013</a>). Shekhawat et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Shekhawat MS, Manokari M, Revathi J (2017) In vitro propagation and ex vitro rooting of Aerva lanata (L.) Juss. ex Schult.: a rare medicinal plant. Indian J Plant Physiol 22:4047. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40502-016-0248-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR160" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1898">2017</a>) reported that a gradual change in the environment of <i>Aerva lanata</i> L. resulted in the acclimatization of young plants in 92%. Kirdmanee et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1995" title="Kirdmanee C, Kitaya Y, Kozai T (1995) Effects of CO2 enrichment and supporting material in vitro on photoautotrophic growth of Eucalyptus plantlets in vitro and ex vitro. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 31:144149. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF02632010&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1905">1995</a>) reported that increased CO<sub>2</sub> levels had a positive effect on the growth and photosynthetic parameters of <i>Eucalyptus</i>. A positive effect was also observed in a herbal <i>Etlingera</i> e<i>latior</i> (Jack) R.M. Smith when a treatment of 1000molmol<sup>1</sup> CO<sub>2</sub>, gas-permeable membranes, and 15g L<sup>1</sup> sucrose was used, resulting in higher fresh and dry mass, better development of veins and palisade and spongy mesophyll, smaller intercellular spaces, and a survival rate of 75% (Pinheiro et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Pinheiro MVM, Ros-Ros AM, da Cruz ACF, Rocha DI, Orbes MY, Saldanha CW, Batista DS, Pinto de Carvalho AC, Otoni WC (2021) CO2 enrichment alters morphophysiology and improves growth and acclimatization in Etlingera Elatior (Jack) R.M. Smith micropropagated plants. Braz  J Bot 44:799809. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40415-021-00741-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR136" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1926">2021</a>). Studies conducted on <i>Vitis Vinifera</i> showed that this acclimatization method had the most significant impact on enhancing acclimatization success (66.67%) (Singh et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Singh NV, Singh SK, Singh AK (2011) Standardization of embryo rescue technique and bio-hardening of grape hybrids (Vitis vinifera L.) using arbuscular mycorrhizal fungi (AMF) under sub-tropical conditions. Vitis 50(3):115118" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR165" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1932">2011</a>). On the other hand, in the case of <i>Senna siamea</i>, a gradual acclimatization was applied simultaneously with spraying the acclimatized plants with  MS nutrient solution (without vitamins) (Parveen et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="Parveen S, Shahzad A, Saema S (2010) In vitro plant regeneration system for Cassia siamea Lam., a leguminous tree of economic importance. Agrofor Syst 80:109116. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10457-010-9301-3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR131" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1939">2010</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">
                           <i>In vitro</i> preconditioning treatments</h3><p>The acclimatization process of plants can be initiated even when the plants grow in vitro, as in <i>Vitex negundo</i> L. (Ahmad and Anis <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Ahmad N, Anis M (2007) Rapid clonal multiplication of a woody tree, Vitex negundo L. through axillary shoots proliferation. Agrofor Syst 71:195200. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1956">2007</a>). Timofeeva et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2014" title="Timofeeva SN, Elkonin LA, Tyrnov VS (2014) Micropropagation of Laburnum anagyroides Medic. through axillary shoot regeneration. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 50:561567. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-014-9618-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR171" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1959">2014</a>) conducted incubation of micropropagated Chaste tree plantlets in non-sterile water for two weeks before the actual acclimatization stage. In vitro acclimatization has been successfully achieved in <i>Olea europaea</i> by using a liquid nutrient medium with vermiculite and perlite (Brito et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Brito G, Costa A, Coelho C, Santos C (2009) Large-scale field acclimatization of Olea maderensis micropropagated plants: morphological and physiological survey. Trees 23:10191031. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00468-009-0344-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1965">2009</a>). It has also been demonstrated that the presence of sucrose in the nutrient medium affects the growth and root formation in plants, but only up to a certain level (dos Santos Rabaiolli et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="dos Santos Rabaiolli SM, Reiniger LRS, Stefanel CM, Buuron da Silva K, Ferreira Paim A, da Fonseca Ziegler AC (2017) Agar does not affect in vitro rhizogenesis and ex vitro acclimatization of Handroanthus chrysotrichus. Cerne 23(2):185192. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/01047760201723022289&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1969">2017</a>). Other studies suggest that lower concentrations of sucrose in the nutrient medium result in better root system quality and plant acclimatization. (Dolcet-Sanjuan et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="Dolcet-Sanjuan R, Claveria E, Camprub A, Estan V, Calvet C (1996) Micropropagation of walnut trees (Juglans regia L.) and response to arbuscular mycorrhizal inoculation. Agronomie 16:639645. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1051/agro:19961008&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1972">1996</a>; Maldaner et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Maldaner J, Nicoloso FT, Santos EC, Fagundes CK, Flores R, Jucoski GO, Skrebsky EC (2007) Crescimento de plntulas de Pfaffia glomerata (Spreng.) Pedersen cultivadas in vitro sob dois nveis de nitrognio e sacarose, durante seis subculturas sucessivas e aclimatizao. Cincia Rural 37:133140. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0103-84782007000100021&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR108" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1975">2007</a>; de Oliveira et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="de Oliveira Y, Pinto F, da Silva ALL, Guedes I, Biasi LA, Quoirin M (2010) An efficient protocol for micropropagation of Melaleuca alternifolia Cheel. Vitr Cell Dev Biol  Plant 46:192197. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-010-9287-6&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1978">2010</a>; Fernandes et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Fernandes D, Souza RS, Costa RB (2013) da cultivo in vitro de teca (Tectona grandis L.f.): uma reviso. Bra J Agric Rev Agric 86:32. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.37856/bja.v86i1.84&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1981">2013</a>). Enrichment of the medium with 30g L<sup>1</sup> sucrose for <i>Melaleuca alternifolia</i> led to 100% acclimatized plants (Maldaner et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Maldaner J, Nicoloso FT, Santos EC, Fagundes CK, Flores R, Jucoski GO, Skrebsky EC (2007) Crescimento de plntulas de Pfaffia glomerata (Spreng.) Pedersen cultivadas in vitro sob dois nveis de nitrognio e sacarose, durante seis subculturas sucessivas e aclimatizao. Cincia Rural 37:133140. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0103-84782007000100021&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR108" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1990">2007</a>). Da Silva et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="da Silva KB, Reiniger LRS, Stefanel CM, dos Santos Rabaiolli SM (2020) Sucrose and substrates on the acclimatization of micropropagated Luehea divaricata plants. Floresta e Amb 27:19. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/2179-8087.117017&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1993">2020</a>) reported a positive effect of sucrose presence in the medium on the acclimatization of <i>Luehea divaricata</i>. Meanwhile, Hoang et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Hoang NN, Kitaya Y, Shibuya T, Endo R (2020) Effects of supporting materials in in vitro acclimatization stage on ex vitro growth of wasabi plants. Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 261:109042. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2019.109042&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e1999">2020</a>), working on the micropropagation of wasabi, used a sucrose-free nutrient medium, considering such a composition as facilitating acclimatization to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions. Chithra et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Chithra M, Martin KP, Sunandakumari C, Madhusoodanan PV (2004) Silver nitrate induced rooting and flowering in vitro on rare rhoeophytic woody medicinal plant. Rotula Aquatica Lour Indian J Biotechnol 3(3):418421" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2006">2004</a>) reported that the use of 2.69M NAA and 11.7M silver nitrate in the medium resulted in 95% acclimatization of strawberry tree explants, with no observed losses even after 3months of transplanting to field conditions. Dos Santos Rabaiolli et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="dos Santos Rabaiolli SM, Reiniger LRS, Stefanel CM, Buuron da Silva K, Ferreira Paim A, da Fonseca Ziegler AC (2017) Agar does not affect in vitro rhizogenesis and ex vitro acclimatization of Handroanthus chrysotrichus. Cerne 23(2):185192. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/01047760201723022289&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2009">2017</a>), found that the use of agar during the in vitro stage can inhibit the root formation and affect the growth of young acclimated plants. On the other hand, Lebedev et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Lebedev V, Arkaev M, Dremova M, Pozdniakov I, Shestibratov K (2018) Effects of growth regulators and gelling agents on ex vitro rooting of raspberry. Plants 8(1):3. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/plants8010003&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2012">2018</a>) reported that reducing agar in the medium led to vitrification of shoots in vitro, negatively impacting acclimatization and delaying raspberry shoot growth. However, vitrification was not observed when agar concentration was reduced in combination with the addition of Phytagel, suggesting that it compensated for the decrease in agar concentration. Clapa et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Clapa D, Fira A, Joshee N (2013) An efficient ex vitro rooting and acclimatization method for horticultural plants using float hydroculture. HortScience 48(9):11591167. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/hortsci.48.9.1159&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2015">2013</a>) developed an effective acclimatization method called float hydroculture, which doesn't require the use of growth-promoting substances (fertilizers, growth regulators, biostimulants) for in vitro-rooted and non-rooted woody plants like <i>Rubus idaeus</i>, cv. Willamette, <i>Ribes nigrum</i> cv. Tisel, <i>Lycium barbarum</i>, or <i>Amelanchier canadensis</i> Rainbow Pillar, where the plants achieved over 80% survival. Another method is <i>ex vitro</i> acclimatization on flow benches with perlite, suitable for many ornamental plant species. The authors suggest this acclimatization method is easy to use and cost-effective, eliminating the need for expensive irrigation systems and phytotrons for acclimatization. Markovic et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Markovic M, Djunisijevic-Bojovic D, Milutinovic M, Petrovic J (2020) Optimisation of a Lawsonia inermis L. micropropagation protocol and acclimatization in a hydroponic culture. Glas Sumar Fak 121:9196. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.2298/GSF2021091M&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR112" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2034">2020</a>), demonstrated the positive effect of grotth regulators (IBA and NAA) and hydroponic nutrient solution (half-strength modified Hoagland nutrient solution changed every 7days) on the acclimatization stage using <i>Lawsonia intermis</i> L. It wasalso proved successful in acclimatizing pear trees by hydroponic treatment, 100% of the plants survived transfer to outdoor environment (Dimitrova and Aleksandrova <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Dimitrova N, Aleksandrova D (2021) Effect of biostimulator Regoplant on acclimatization of micropropagated GiselA 6 cherry rootstock in floating system. Sci Pap Ser B Hortic LXIV:4955." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2040">2021</a>). Erst et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Erst A, Novikova TI, Karkulov A, Zaytseva Y (2012) Adaptation of regenerants Rhododendron hybridum to ex vitro conditions. Sci Bull BSU 9 (128: 8). Belgorod State Univ., Belgorod." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2044">2012</a>) reported that 20-day adaptation through acclimatization of <i>Rhododendron hybridum</i> in a hydroponic nutrient solution enabled the development of plants with well-developed root systems. Studies on <i>Camellia sinensis</i> L. showed that using larger containers (500ml conical flask) and an extended incubation time in the growth chamber (12weeks instead of 4) significantly increased the number of acclimatized plants (Bag et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="Bag N, Palni LMS, Nandi SK (2019) An efficient method for acclimatization: in vitro hardening of tissue culture-raised tea plants [Camellia sinensis (L.) O. Kuntze]. Curr Sci 117(2):288293" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2053">2019</a>). To minimize acclimatization stress in Dragons Blood plantlets, 14-day pre-acclimatization period was underwent. Afterward, plants were transferred to a greenhouse and kept under 70% shading for 60days. Pre-acclimatization allowed the plants to thrive in the greenhouse without wilting, yellowing, or drying out (Oliveira Jnior et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Oliveira Jnior JB, de Pessoa CMP, Lopes H, da S Costa FH, Pereira JES (2020) Protocol for development of zygotic embryos in vitro and acclimatization of Dragons Blood plantlets. Res Soc Dev 9(9). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.33448/rsd-v9i9.7031&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR125" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2056">2020</a>). Inthe studies on acclimatization of walnut trees, it was found that lowering relative humidity (application of KCl for 2 and 4weeks before transferring the micropropagated plantlets to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions) in the growth vessels effectively increased the efficiency of <i>ex vitro</i> acclimatization (Asayesh et al. 2017). Research on <i>Vaccinium ashei</i> Reade showed that equipment with membrane-vented polypropylene lids during growth in vitro contributed to increased plant survival and had positive effects on subsequent acclimatization of micropropagated plantlets (Hung et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016a" title="Hung CD, Hong CH, Kim SK, Lee KH, Cao PJY, Cao DD, Nam MW, Choi DH, Lee, HI (2016a) In vitro proliferation and ex vitro rooting of microshoots of commercially important rabbiteye blueberry (Vaccinium ashei Reade) using spectral lights. Sci Hortic 211:248254. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2016.09.003&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2069">2016a</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference b" title="Hung CD, Hong CH, Kim SK, Lee KH, Park JY, Nam MW, Choi DH, Lee HI (2016b) LED light for in vitro and ex vitro efficient growth of economically important highbush blueberry (Vaccinium corymbosum L.). Acta Physiol Plant 38:19. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11738-016-2164-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2072">b</a>). Cui et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="Cui Y, Deng Y, Zheng K, Hu X, Zhu M, Deng X, Xi R (2019) An efficient micropropagation protocol for an endangered ornamental tree species (Magnolia sirindhorniae Noot. &amp; Chalermglin) and assessment of genetic uniformity through DNA markers. Sci Rep 9:9634. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-019-46050-w&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2075">2019</a>) acclimatized <i>Magnolia</i> by keeping rooted microplants in the jars by approximately 57days in the greenhouse whereas by preconditioning plants were kept in sterilized medium (peat and soil), acclimation rate was 90.2%.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Simultaneous acclimatization and rooting, substrates dedicated to acclimatization</h3><p>A common practice in the acclimatization of woody plants is to combine it with rooting. Rooting plants <i>ex vitro</i> ensures a more extensive root system, and these plants do not require additional acclimatization before transferring them to the greenhouse (Pruski et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2000" title="Pruski KW, Lewis T, Astatkie T, Nowak J (2000) Micropropagation of chokecherry and pincherry cultivars. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 63:93100. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1006461423373&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR143" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2092">2000</a>; Borkowska <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2001" title="Borkowska B (2001) Morphological and physiological characteristics of micropropagated strawberry plants rooted in vitro or ex vitro. Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 89(3):195206. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/S0304-4238(00)00230-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2095">2001</a>; Shekhawat et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Shekhawat MS, Manokari M, Revathi J (2017) In vitro propagation and ex vitro rooting of Aerva lanata (L.) Juss. ex Schult.: a rare medicinal plant. Indian J Plant Physiol 22:4047. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40502-016-0248-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR160" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2098">2017</a>; Leva <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Leva A (2011) Innovative protocol for ex vitro rooting on olive micropropagation. Open Life Sci 6:352358. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.2478/s11535-011-0010-3&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2101">2011</a>; Erst et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Erst A, Gorbunov A, Karakulov A (2018) Rooting and acclimatization of in vitro propagated microshoots of the Ericaceae. J Appl Hortic 20(30):177181. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.37855/jah.2018.v20i03.31&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2105">2018</a>). Experiments on shrubs in the <i>Ericaceae</i> family have shown that rooting during acclimatization is effective for plants in the <i>Rhododendron</i>genus (Erst et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Erst A, Gorbunov A, Karakulov A (2018) Rooting and acclimatization of in vitro propagated microshoots of the Ericaceae. J Appl Hortic 20(30):177181. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.37855/jah.2018.v20i03.31&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2114">2018</a>). A similar effect was observed in <i>Acacia crassicarpa</i>, where the time interval between preparing cuttings and placing them in the nursery and the family of the plant influenced <i>ex vitro</i> rooting (Suharyanto et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Sivanandhan G, Kapil Dev G, Jeyaraj M, Rajesh M, Muthuselvam M, Selvaraj N, Manickavasagam M, Ganapathi A (2013) A promising approach on biomass accumulation and with anolides production in cell suspension culture of Withania somnifera (L.) Dunal. Protoplasma 250(4):885898" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR167" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2124">2016</a>). Successful <i>ex vitro</i> rooting has also been applied to <i>Ulmus minor</i> Mill. (Conde et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Conde P, Sousa A, Costa A, Santos CA (2007) Protocol for Ulmus minor Mill. micropropagation and acclimatization. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 92:113119" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2133">2007</a>) and <i>Rubus ideaus</i> L. (Robres-Torres et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2015" title="Reed BM (1995) Screening Pyrus germplasm for in vitro rooting response. HortScience 30:12921294. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTSCI.30.6.1292&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR151" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2139">2015</a>). Clapa (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Clapa D (2007) Tissue culture and ex vitro acclimation of Rhododendron sp. Bull Univ Agric Sci Vet Med Cluj-Napoca Hortic 64:3943" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2143">2007</a>) suggests that it may be beneficial to skip in vitro rooting in favor of rooting during acclimatization, using <i>Rhododendron</i> as an example. Rathore et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Rathore JS, Rathore V, Shekhawat NS, Singh RP, Liler G, Phulwaria M, Dagla HR (2004) Micropropagation of woody plants. Plant Biotechnol Molec Markers, pp 195205. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/1-4020-3213-7_13&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR147" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2149">2004</a>) showed that <i>Balanites aegyptiaca</i>, <i>Citrus limon</i>, and <i>Syzygium cumini</i> rooted during acclimatization adapted more easily to field conditions than the same plants rooted in vitro. <i>Lycium barbarum</i> L. can be successfully rooted during acclimatization with the use of IBA and putrescine (Silvestri et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Silvestri C, Sabbatini G, Marangelli F, Rugini E, Cristofori V (2018) Micropropagation and ex vitro rooting of wolfberry. Hort Sci 53(10):14941499. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTSCI13423-18&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR164" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2165">2018</a>). Conversely, honeysuckle (<i>Lonicera caerulea</i>) rooted in glass had a higher survival rate (up to 88%) compared to plants rooted <i>ex vitro</i> (Wojtania et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Wojtania A, Markiewicz M, Graj-Koniarska J (2020) Ex vitro rooting, acclimatization and genetic stability of Lonicera caerulea var. kamtschatica. J Hortic Res 28:6170. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.2478/johr-2020-0019&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR177" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2174">2020</a>). From an economic standpoint, plant survival must exceed 60% (Pence <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Pence VC (2011) Evaluating costs for the in vitro propagation and preservation of endangered plants. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 47:176187. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-010-9323-6&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR133" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2177">2011</a>; Tisarum et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Tisarum R, Samphumphung T, Theerawitaya C, Prommee W, Cha-um S (2018) In vitro photoautotrophic acclimatization, direct transplantation and ex vitro adaptation of rubber tree (Hevea brasiliensis). Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 133:215223. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-017-1374-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR172" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2181">2018</a>). Therefore, acclimatization of in vitro unrooted strawberry tree plants has proven uneconomical. Even treating unrooted plants with IBA solutions (5002000ppm) did not ensure economic feasibility (Mereti et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2002" title="Mereti M, Grigoriadou K, Nanos GD (2002) Micropropagation of the strawberry tree. Arbutus Unedo l Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 93:143148. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/S0304-4238(01)00330-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2184">2002</a>). In contrast, micropropagated strawberry tree seedlings (<i>Arbutus unedo</i> L.) rooted in glass acclimatized at rates of 8594.4% (Gomes and Canhoto <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Gomes F, Canhoto JM (2009) Micropropagation of strawberry tree (Arbutus unedo L.) from adult plants. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 45:7282. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-008-9164-8&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2190">2009</a>). Similarly, the shrub <i>Rotula aquatica</i> Lour., where plants rooted in glass with addition of 2.69M NAA, acclimatized at a rate of 80%, while those rooted <i>ex vitro</i> acclimatized at 65% (Martin <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Martin K (2003) Rapid in vitro multiplication and ex vitro rooting of Rotula aquatica Lour., a rare rhoeophytic woody medicinal plant. Plant Cell Rep 21:415420. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00299-002-0547-8&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR113" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2200">2003</a>). However, immersion of unrooted micropropagated plants for 25days in a solution of 2.69M NAA and 11.7M silver nitrate resulted in 90% plant survival (Chithra et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Chithra M, Martin KP, Sunandakumari C, Madhusoodanan PV (2004) Silver nitrate induced rooting and flowering in vitro on rare rhoeophytic woody medicinal plant. Rotula Aquatica Lour Indian J Biotechnol 3(3):418421" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2203">2004</a>). Rooted <i>Prunus serotina</i> (in glass with 2.510M IBA) acclimatized at rates of 7684% (Liu and Pijut <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Liu X, Pijut PM (2008) Plant regeneration from in vitro leaves of mature black cherry (Prunus serotina). Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 94:113123. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-008-9393-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR106" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2209">2008</a>). <i>Albizia lebbeck</i> L. acclimatized in a soil and sand mixture (1:1) at 60% (Al-Joboury <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Al-Joboury KR (2012) In vitro propagation of Albizia lebbeck through axillary bud culture indroduction. Ibn Al-Haitham J Pure Appl Sci 25(1):17" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2215">2012</a>; Chatterjee and Ghosh <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Chatterjee T, Ghosh B (2020) Micropropagation of medicinal plants: a review. Int J Econ Plants 7:6672. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10529-010-0290-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2219">2020</a>). <i>Celastrus paniculatus</i> successfully acclimatized, with a 70% survival rate during acclimatization and transfer to field conditions (Lal and Singh <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="Lal D, Singh N (2010) Mass multiplication of Celastrus paniculatus Willd: an important medicinal plant under in vitro conditions via nodal segments. Int J Biodivers Conserv 2(6):140145" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2225">2010</a>). The success of acclimatization is also influenced by the substrate used during acclimatization. Rooted sumac seedlings <i>(Rhus coriaria</i> L.) in a substrate of perlite:peat moss:soil (2:1:3) survived acclimatization at a rate of 870.5% (Amiri and Mohammadi <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Amiri S, Mohammadi R (2021) Establishment of an efficient in vitro propagation protocol for sumac (Rhus coriaria L.) and confirmation of the genetic homogeneity. Sci Rep 11:173. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-020-80550-4&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2231">2021</a>). E<i>urycoma longifolia</i> acclimatifzed at a 100% rate in Jiffy substrate (Yahya et al. 2015), and <i>Populus</i> x <i>euramericana</i> 'Neva' acclimatized at over 80% in vermiculite:high peat (1:1) substrate (Zheng et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Zheng W, Xu XD, Dai H, Chen LQ (2009) Direct regeneration of plants derived from in vitro cultured shoot tips and leaves of three Lysimachia species. Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 122(1):138141. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2009.03.018&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR188" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2244">2009</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">The effect of light on acclimatization</h3><p>Higher light intensity stimulates the growth of young leaves that are adapted to autotrophy from the start. Therefore, the significant effect of the light environment on the success of the acclimatization stage of in vitro-propagated plants is described (Jagieo-Kubiec et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021a" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, Ilczuk A, ukaszewska AJ (2021) Optimizing micropropagation conditions for a recalcitrant ninebark (Physocarpus opulifolius L. maxim.) cultivar. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 57:281295. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-020-10154-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2255">2021a</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference b" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, ukaszewska AJ, Pacholczak A (2021b) Acclimation to ex vitro conditions in ninebark. Agronomy 11(4):612. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11040612&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2258">b</a>). Increased light intensity during the acclimatization stage accelerates the growth of young, fully autotrophic leaves (Donnelly and Vidaver <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1984" title="Donnelly DJ, Vidaver WE (1984) Pigment content and gas exchange of red raspberry in vitro and ex vitro. J Am Soc Hortic Sci 109:177181. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/JASHS.109.2.177&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2261">1984</a>). An increase in photon flux in <i>Gevuina avellana</i> resulted in significant improvements in fluorescence parameters such as photochemical quenching, non-photochemical quenching, electron transport rate, and photochemical efficiency of PSII, compared to ventilation and control treatments (Alvarez et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Alvarez C, Sez P, Sez K, Snchez-Olate M, Ros D (2012) Effects of light and ventilation on physiological parameters during in vitro acclimatization of Gevuina avellana mol. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 110:93101. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-012-0133-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2267">2012</a>). Dias et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Dias MC, Pinto G, Santos C (2011) Acclimatization of micropropagated plantlets induces an antioxidative burst: a case study with Ulmus minor Mill. Photosynthetica 49:259266. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11099-011-0028-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2271">2011</a>) demonstrated that illuminating with artificial light at an appropriate intensity (100molm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>1</sup>) during the acclimatization stage reduces oxidative stress compared to higher-intensity light. Generally, LL (Low Light) caused less electrolyte leakage, lower levels of MDA, and higher activities of CAT. In contrast, in <i>Rauvolfia tetraphylla</i>, applying higher light intensity (300molm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>1</sup>) significantly improved the net photosynthetic rate but resulted in increased electrolyte leakage, lower CAT activity, and higher APX activity on the 28th day compared to 50molm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>1</sup> light levels (Faisal and Anis <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Faisal M, Anis M (2009) Changes in photosynthetic activity, pigment composition, electrolyte leakage, lipid peroxidation, and antioxidant enzymes during ex vitro establishment of micropropagated Rauvolfia tetraphylla plantlets. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 99:125132. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-009-9584-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2290">2009</a>). It has been found that using of LEDs as a light source during the development of microshoots in vitro, as well as in post-adaptation, increases the rate of plant development (Dutta Gupta and Agarwal <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Dutta Gupta S, Agarwal A (2017) Influence of LED lighting on in vitro plant regeneration and associated cellular redox balance. In: Dutta Gupta S (eds) Light emitting diodes for agriculture. Springer, Singapore. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/978-981-10-5807-3_12&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2293">2017</a>; Hung et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016a" title="Hung CD, Hong CH, Kim SK, Lee KH, Cao PJY, Cao DD, Nam MW, Choi DH, Lee, HI (2016a) In vitro proliferation and ex vitro rooting of microshoots of commercially important rabbiteye blueberry (Vaccinium ashei Reade) using spectral lights. Sci Hortic 211:248254. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2016.09.003&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2296">2016a</a><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016b" title="Hung CD, Hong CH, Kim SK, Lee KH, Park JY, Nam MW, Choi DH, Lee HI (2016b) LED light for in vitro and ex vitro efficient growth of economically important highbush blueberry (Vaccinium corymbosum L.). Acta Physiol Plant 38:19. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11738-016-2164-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2298">2016b</a>). Acclimatized <i>Vaccinium ashei</i> under LED with an 80% red and 20% blue ratio resulted in increased biometric parameters and chlorophyll accumulation (Hung et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016b" title="Hung CD, Hong CH, Kim SK, Lee KH, Park JY, Nam MW, Choi DH, Lee HI (2016b) LED light for in vitro and ex vitro efficient growth of economically important highbush blueberry (Vaccinium corymbosum L.). Acta Physiol Plant 38:19. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11738-016-2164-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2305">2016b</a>). Chung et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Chung GJ, Lee JH, Oh MM (2020) Growth and acclimation of in vitro-propagated M9 apple rootstock plantlets under various visible light spectrums. Agronomy 10(7):1017. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy10071017&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2308">2020</a>), exploring the acclimatization of apple rootstocks, demonstrated the positive impact of red light on photosynthesis intensity and biomass growth, while the presence of blue light was an appropriate source to increase chlorophyll content and stomatal conductance. Akimova et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2022" title="Akimova S, Radzhabov A, Esaulko A, Samoshenkov E, Nechiporenko I, Kazakov P, Voskoboinikov Y, Matsneva A, Zubkov A, Aisanov T (2022) Improvement of ex vitro growing completion of highbush blueberry (Vaccinium corymbosum L.) in containers. Forests 13(10):1550. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/f13101550&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2311">2022</a>) showed that LED light positively affects the growth and development of <i>Vaccinium corymbosum</i> L. in the early stages of acclimatization. The use of a reversed photoperiod (16h of darkness/8h of light) in <i>Alangium salviifolium</i> (L.f.) was crucial in inducing root formation (Pandey et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2022" title="Pandey A, Verma O, Chand S (2022) In vitro propagation of Alangium salviifolium (L. f.) Wangerin: an important tropical medicinal tree. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 148:1522. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-021-02155-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR130" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2321">2022</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Exogenous use of various plant growth regulators in the acclimatization of woody plants</h3><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec11">Antitranspirants</h4><p>Antitranspirants can be of natural and synthetic origin. Their application can act as a protective barrier by reducing leaf temperature, reflecting sunlight, or assisting in the closure of stomata (Plaut et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Plaut Z, Magril Y, Kedem U (2004) A new film forming material, which reduces water vapour conductance more than CO2 fixation in several horticultural crops. J Hortic Sci Biotechnol 79:528532. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/14620316.2004.11511800&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR138" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2337">2004</a>; Dinis et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Dinis LT, Ferreira H, Pinto G, Bernardo S, Correia Moutinho-Pereira CM (2016) Kaolin-based, foliar reflective film protects photosystem II structure and function in grapevine leaves exposed to heat and high solar radiation. Photosynthetica 54:4755. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11099-015-0156-8&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2340">2016</a>; Moroni et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Moroni FJ, Gascon-Aldana PJ, Rogiers SY (2020) Characterizing the efficacy of a film-forming antitranspirant on raspberry foliar and fruit transpiration. Biology (Basel) 9(9):255. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/biology9090255&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2343">2020</a>). Panapitiya et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Panapitiya PDDM, Priyadarshan AIS, Amarasinghe VLP, Leelarathne NDCSD (2021) In vitro hardening of Dendrobium plantlets to enhance acclimatization. In: International conference on applied and pure sciences, 2020. Faculty of Science, University of Kelaniya, Sri Lanka. 3." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR129" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2346">2021</a>) reports that enriching the nutrient medium with a 0.10mg L<sup>1</sup> PBZ (Paclobutrazol) of <i>Dendrobium</i> resulted in a 13% higher rate of acclimatized plants compared to the control and improved biometric parameters. Hazarika and Parthasarathy, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2002" title="Hazarika BN, Parthasarathy VA (2002) Effects of reduced humidity and antitranspirants in acclimatizing micropropagated Citrus plantlets. J Appl Hortic 4(1):3032. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.37855/jah.2002.v04i01.09&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2355">2002</a>) demonstrated the positive effect of 8-hydroxyquinoline (8 HQ) in conc. Of 2mg L<sup>1</sup> in <i>Citrus</i>, which had a favorable impact on the relative water content (RWC) and the survival of acclimatized plants (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#Tab3">3</a>). Abscisic acid (ABA) plays a significant role in regulating various processes in plants. Under non-stressful conditions, the level of this hormone remains low. It significantly increases in response to stresful conditions due to biotic and abiotic stresses or during seed maturation (Xiong and Zhu <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Xiong L, Zhu JK (2003) Regulation of abscisic acid biosynthesis. Plant Physiol 133(1):2936. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1104/pp.103.025395&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR180" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2366">2003</a>; Rai et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Rai MK, Shekhawat NS, Harish GAK, Phulwaria M, Ram K, Jaiswal U (2011) The role of abscisic acid in plant tissue culture: a review of recent progress. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 106:179190. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-011-9923-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR145" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2370">2011</a>). Endogenous ABA plays a role in regulating water status by osmotic closure of stomata in response to abiotic stresses such as salinity, drought, and low temperature (Xiong and Zhu <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Xiong L, Zhu JK (2003) Regulation of abscisic acid biosynthesis. Plant Physiol 133(1):2936. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1104/pp.103.025395&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR180" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2373">2003</a>; Schwartz et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Schwartz SH, Qin X, Zeevaart JAD (2003) Elucidation of the indirect pathway of abscisic acid biosynthesis by mutants, genes, and enzymes. Plant Physiol 131(4):15911601. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1104/pp.102.017921&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR157" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2376">2003</a>; Tuteja <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Tuteja N (2007) Abscisic acid and abiotic stress signaling. Plant Signal Behav 2(3):135138. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.4161/psb.2.3.4156&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR173" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2379">2007</a>; Rai et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Rai MK, Shekhawat NS, Harish GAK, Phulwaria M, Ram K, Jaiswal U (2011) The role of abscisic acid in plant tissue culture: a review of recent progress. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 106:179190. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-011-9923-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR145" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2382">2011</a>). Exogenous ABA influences the adaptation and acclimatization as a means to inhibit excessive transpiration when stomata are not functioning. It contributes to an increase in the chlorophyll content and other photosynthesis parameters in plants (Pospsilovet al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2007" title="Pospilov J, Synkov H, Haisel D, Semordov  (2007) Acclimation of plantlets to ex vitro conditions: Effects of air humidity, irradiance, CO2 concentration and abscisic acid (a review). Acta Hortic 748:2938. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.17660/ActaHortic.2007.748.2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR141" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2385">2007</a>; <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1999" title="Pospsilov J, Ticha I, Kadlecek P, Haisel D, Plzakova S (1999) Acclimatization of micropropagated plants to ex vitro conditions. Biol Plant 42:481497. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1023/A:1002688208758&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2389">1999</a>; Rai et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Rai MK, Shekhawat NS, Harish GAK, Phulwaria M, Ram K, Jaiswal U (2011) The role of abscisic acid in plant tissue culture: a review of recent progress. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 106:179190. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11240-011-9923-9&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR145" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2392">2011</a>). Huh et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Huh YS, Lee JK, Nam SY (2017) Improvement of ex vitro acclimatization of mulberry plantlets by supplement of abscisic acid to the last subculture medium. J Plant Biotechnol 44:431437. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.5010/JPB.2017.44.4.431&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2395">2017</a>) demonstrated that mulberry microshoots treated with ABA prior acclimatization had a higher chl a and b content, higher RWC, net photosynthetic rate, lower transpiration rate and stomatal conductance compared to control plants. After 1month of acclimatization, 85.6% of ABA-treated plants survived, while the survival rate of untreated plants was 56.8%. Jagieo-Kubiec et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021a" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, Ilczuk A, ukaszewska AJ (2021) Optimizing micropropagation conditions for a recalcitrant ninebark (Physocarpus opulifolius L. maxim.) cultivar. Vitr Cell Dev Biol Plant 57:281295. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s11627-020-10154-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2398">2021a</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference b" title="Jagieo-Kubiec K, Nowakowska K, ukaszewska AJ, Pacholczak A (2021b) Acclimation to ex vitro conditions in ninebark. Agronomy 11(4):612. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11040612&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2401">b</a>), studying ninebark (<i>Physocarpus opulifolius</i> L. Maxim.), found that ABA apraying had a positive effect on the acclimatization, ensuring adaptation in 93% of cases. A decrease in transpiration rate and stomatal conductance was observed, along with an increase in chl a+b and Cx+c content. Nowakowska et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Nowakowska K, Nongdam P, Samsurizal NA, Pacholczak A (2023) An efficient micropropagation protocol for the endangered European shrub February daphne (Daphne mezereum L.) and Identification of bacteria in culture. Agriculture 13(9):1692. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agriculture13091692&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR123" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2408">2023</a>) on <i>Daphne mezereum</i> reported that 70% of acclimatized plants survived by ABA treatment, while in the control, the rate was 45%. On the other hand, Rattanpal and Prakash, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2015" title="Rattanpal HS, Prakash O (2015) Studies on in vitro regeneration and acclimatization of rough lemon. Indian J Ecol 42(1):117121" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR148" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e2414">2015</a>) showed that <i>Citrus</i> treated with 10mg L<sup>1</sup> ABA did not result in a higher percentage of survived plants (mean of all concentrations=31%), while treatment with 500mL L<sup>1</sup> glycerol resulted in 76.7% rate.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-3"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab3" data-test="table-caption">Table3 Recent reports on treatments facilitating acclimatization of woody plants</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1/tables/3" aria-label="Full size table 3"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec12">Auxins</h4><p>Auxins (AUX) are the primary regulators of plant growth and development. They play a significant role in controlling plant tropisms and serve as regulators in various plant developmental processes, including cell division, growth, and differentiation (Frick and Strader <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Frick EM, Strader LC (2018) Roles for IBA-derived auxin in plant development. J Exp Bot 69:169177. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/jxb/erx298&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3462">2018</a>; Zhao <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Zhao Y (2018) Essential roles of local auxin biosynthesis in plant development and in adaptation to environmental changes. Annu Rev Plant Biol 69:417435. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1146/annurev-arplant-042817-040226&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR187" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3465">2018</a>; Gallei and Luschnig <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Gaidamashvili M, Benelli C (2021) Threatened woody plants of georgia and micropropagation as a tool for in vitro conservation. Agronomy 11(6):120. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/agronomy11061082&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3468">2020</a>). Exogenous application of AUX supports and accelerates the rooting of seedlings (Zhang et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Zhang W, Fan J, Tan Q, Zhou T, Cao F (2017) The effects of exogenous hormones on rooting process and the activities of key enzymes of Malus hupehensis stem cuttings. PLoS ONE 12(2):e0172320. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pone.0172320&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR186" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3471">2017</a>). Skirvin and Sriskandarajah, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1993" title="Skirvin RM, Sriskandarajah S (1993) The use of fogging and phototron units to acclimatize in vitro-derived apple shoots. Horttechnology 3:208210. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTTECH.3.2.208&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR168" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3474">1993</a>) reported that adding IBA (2mg L<sup>1</sup>) to the nutrient medium results in the highest survival rate and biometric parameters for subsequently acclimatized apple plants. Similarly, Hunkova and Gajdoov (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="Hunkov J, Gajdoov A (2019) In vitro rooting and acclimatization of Amelanchier alnifolia (Nutt.) Nutt. ex M. Roem: testing of auxin, spermidine, and gibberellin for overcoming dormancy. J Berry Res 9(3):549561. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3233/JBR-180376&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3480">2019</a>) reported that AUX in the nutrient medium promotes rooting and acclimatization of <i>Amelanchier alnifolia</i> (Nutt.). According to urkovi (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="urkovi J (2008) Micropropagation of mature Cornus mas Macrocarpa. Trees 22:597602. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00468-008-0228-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3486">2008</a>), NAA in the medium at various concentrations not only enhances plant rooting frequency, but also has a positive effect on the acclimatization of <i>Cornus mas</i> 'Macrocarpa' plants. The effectiveness of that treatment before placing in the substrate has been confirmed in many woody plants, such as <i>Acer, Betula, Malus, Balanites, Citrus, and Syzygium</i> (McClelland et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1990" title="McClelland MT, Smith MAL, Carothers ZB (1990) The effects of in vitro and ex vitro root initiation on subsequent microcutting root quality in three woody plants. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 23:115123. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF00035831&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR114" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3496">1990</a>). Zaytseva et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Zaytseva YG, Ambros EV, Novikova TI (2018) Rooting and acclimatization to ex vitro conditions of regenerants of frost-resistant members of Rhododendron. Turczaninowia 21(1):144152" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR185" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3499">2018</a>) reported that application of IBA during the acclimatization stage of R<i>hododendron</i> plants affected beneficially. The 'Helsinki University' variety achieved 100% rooting, <i>R. mucronulatum</i>89%, <i>R. sichotense</i>84%, and <i>R. schlippenbachii</i>60%). However, Muraseva and Kostikova, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Muraseva D, Kostikova V (2020) In vitro and ex vitro rooting of Spiraea betulifolia subsp. aemiliana (Rosaceae), an ornamental shrub. BIO Web Conf. 24. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1051/bioconf/20202400058&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3515">2020</a>) reported that for <i>Spiraea betulifolia</i> subsp. <i>aemiliana</i>, treated with 400mg L<sup>1</sup> of IAA (treatment time3.5h) or 200mg L<sup>1</sup> succinic acid (exposure 16h) proved ineffective for root formation in plants acclimatized <i>ex vitro</i>. Oakes et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Oakes AD, Pilkey HC, Powell WA (2020) Improving ex vitro rooting and acclimatization techniques for micropropagated american chestnut. J Environ Hortic 38(4):149157. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.24266/0738-2898-38.4.149&#xA;                  &#xA;                ." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR124" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3532">2020</a>) stated that immersing microshoots of <i>Castanea dentala</i> (American Chestnut) in a 31mg L<sup>1</sup> IBA solution increased the number of roots in plants, thereby influencing the success of the acclimatization stage. Pelizza et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Pelizza TR, Muniz J, Camargo P, Kretzschmar AA, Rufato L (2013) Enraizamento ex vitro e aclimatizao de plntulas micropropagadas de amoreira-preta Xavante. Rev Bras Frutic 35:329332. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/S0100-29452013000100039&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR132" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3540">2013</a>) also demonstrated that immersing micropropagated blackberry seedlings in 320mg L<sup>1</sup> IBA for 5min had a positive impact on the root formation during acclimatization. Silvestri et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Silvestri C, Sabbatini G, Marangelli F, Rugini E, Cristofori V (2018) Micropropagation and ex vitro rooting of wolfberry. Hort Sci 53(10):14941499. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTSCI13423-18&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR164" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3545">2018</a>) reported that the use of it promotes rooting (up to 95.2%) and acclimatization (88.795.1%) of Goji berries. Soaking unrooted microshoots of <i>Simmondsia chinensis</i> (Link) Schneider in 500mg L<sup>1</sup> IBA for 3min resulted in 98.4% of rooted and acclimatized plants (Bala et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="Bala R, Laura JS, Beniwal VS (2019) Efficient in vitro shoot regeneration and ex vitro rooting in simmondsia direct adventitious shoot bud regeneration and ex vitro rooting in leaf explants of female Simmondsia chinensis (link) Schneideran important industrial shrub. Asian J Microbiol Biotech Environ Sci 21(2):448454" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3554">2019</a>). Unrooted microshoots of <i>Bauhinia racemosa</i> Lam. with 400mg L<sup>1</sup> IBA achieved an 85% acclimatization rate (Sharma et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Sharma U, Kataria V, Shekhawat NS (2017) In vitro propagation, ex vitro rooting and leaf micromorphology of Bauhinia racemosa Lam.: a leguminous tree with medicinal values. Physiol Mol Biol Plants 23:969977. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s12298-017-0459-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR159" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3562">2017</a>).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec13">Brassinosteroids</h4><p>Brassinosteroids (BRs) are plant hormones essential for plant growth and development, playing a significant role in plant growth, development, and stress tolerance (Janeczko <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2005" title="Janeczko A (2005) Brasinosteroidy w rolnictwie, ogrodnictwie i kulturach in vitro. Kosmos 54(23):259265" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3573">2005</a>). They are found in all plant tissues, with the highest concentration in fruits, seeds, and pollen grains (Fujioka et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1997" title="Fujioka S, Li J, Choi YH, Seto H, Takatsuto S, Noguchi T, Watanabe T, Kuriyama H, Yokota T, Chory J, Sakurai A (1997) The Arabidopsis deetiolated mutant is blocked early in brassinosteroid biosynthesis. Plant Cell 9(11):19511962. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1105/tpc.9.11.1951&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3576">1997</a>; Li and He <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Li Z, He Y (2020) Roles of brassinosteroids in plant reproduction. Int J Mol Sci 21:872. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/ijms21030872&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3579">2020</a>). BRs are essential components for plant tissue growth and are especially important for plants to complete their life cycle successfully, interacting with auxin to promote root development (Bao et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2004" title="Bao F, Shen J, Brady SR, Mudas GK, Asami T, Yang Z (2004) Brassinosteroids interact with auxin to promote lateral root development in arabidopsis. Plant Physiol 134(4):16241631. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1104/pp.103.036897&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3582">2004</a>). They regulate various aspects of plant growth and development (Nolan et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Nolan TM, Vukainovi N, Liu D, Russinova E, Yin Y (2020) Brassinosteroids: multidimensional regulators of plant growth, development, and stress responses. Plant Cell 32:295318. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1105/tpc.19.00335&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR122" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3585">2020</a>). BRs also play a crucial role in plant adaptation to new environmental conditions (Kagale et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2006" title="Kagale S, Divi UK, Krochko JE, Keller WA, Krishn P (2006) Brassinosteroid confers tolerance in Arabidopsis thaliana and Brassica napus to a range of abiotic stresses. Planta 225:353364. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00425-006-0361-6&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3589">2006</a>; Rajewska et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2016" title="Rajewska I, Talarek M, Bajguz A (2016) Brassinosteroids and response of plants to heavy metals action. Front. Plant Sci 7. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3389/fpls.2016.00629&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR146" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3592">2016</a>; Xia et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Xia XJ, Fang PP, Guo X, Qian X, Zhou J, Shi K, Zhou YH, Yu JQ (2018) Brassinosteroid-mediated apoplastic H2O2glutaredoxin 12/14 cascade regulates antioxidant capacity in response to chilling in tomato. Plant Cell Environ 41(5):10521064. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/pce.13052&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR179" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3595">2018</a>; Ahammed et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Ahammed GJ, Li X, Liu A, Chen S (2020) Brassinosteroids in plant tolerance to abiotic stress. J Plant Growth Regul 39:14511464. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3598">2020</a>), suggesting their potential utility in acclimatizing in vitro propagated plants. Importantly, BRs exhibit physiological activity at concentrations approximately 1000 times lower than other plant hormones. In in vitro cultures, BRs promote callus growth and stimulate both indirect and direct embryogenesis and organogenesis, such as shoot regeneration and growth. Numerous studies on various plant species have confirmed that adding BRs to the nutrient medium supports the propagation of explants. Pullman et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2003" title="Pullman GS, Zhang Y, Phan BH (2003) Brassinolide improves embryogenic tissue initiation in conifers and rice. Plant Cell Rep 22:96104. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00299-003-0674-x&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR144" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3601">2003</a>) found embryogenesis stimulation in fir, spruce, and pine cultures on media containing brassinolide. Yue et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Yue J, Fu Z, Zhang L, Zhang Z, Zhang J (2018) The positive effect of different 24-epiBL pretreatments on salinity tolerance in Robinia pseudoacacia L. Seedl Forests 10(1):4. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/f10010004&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR184" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3604">2018</a>) reported a positive impact of using 24-epibrassinolide on <i>Robinia pseudoacacia</i> L. seedlings exposed to salt stress. Adding 5mg L<sup>1</sup> of brassinolide to the medium supported sugarcane acclimatization, leading to higher survival rates, shoot length, leaf count, and fresh mass.
