The application of BL might affect plant growth stimulation directly or by enhancing the action of auxin and cytokinin in the medium (Chavan et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Chavan CS, Chavan SS, Velhal RS, Patil AG, Desgmukh LP, Bapat VA (2018) Effect of Brassinolide on in vitro growth of sugarcane Co 86032 (Saccharum spp.). AIP Conference Proceedings. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1063/1.5047722&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3613">2018</a>). The efficacy of a brassinosteroid analog (Biobras-16) during the acclimatization stage of minicutting-propagated <i>Psidium</i> seedlings has already been demonstrated. The application of BB-16 at concentrations between 0.3 and 0.6mg L<sup>1</sup> stimulated seedling growth and allowed for the production of high-quality plants in a short time (Arantes et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Arantes de Souza MB, Sales MC, de Menezes de Assis Gomes M, Ferreira dos Santos R, Pereira Galvao S, Pulitini Vaz G, (2020) Brassinosteroid accelerates the growth of Psidium hybrid during acclimatization of seedlings obtained from minicuttings. Pesqui Agropecuria Trop 50:18. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1590/1983-40632020v5064743&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3621">2020</a>). Application of Biobras-16 on pineapple during acclimatization (0.1mg L<sup>1</sup>) resulted in 2.8 times greater dry mass production compared to untreated plants (Catunda et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2008" title="Catunda PHA, Marinho CS, Gomes MM, de A, Carvalho, AJC (2008) Brassinosteride e substratos na aclimatizao do abacaxizeiro Imperial. Acta Sci Agron, 30. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.4025/actasciagron.v30i3.3512&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3627">2008</a>). The application of 0.0096mg L<sup>1</sup> brassinolide facilitated more efficient growth and acclimatization of <i>Rubus idaeus</i> L. Microshoots, ensuring better acclimatization and adaptation to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions (Robres-Torres et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2015" title="Robres-Torres E, Lpz-Medina J, Rocha-Granados MC (2015) Adventitious shoot elongation of raspberry (Rubus idaeus L.) is influenced by brassinosteroids. Rev Mex Ciencias Agrcolas 6(5):991999" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR152" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3638">2015</a>).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec14">Jasmonic acid</h4><p>Jasmonic acid (JA) as another plant hormone is known to induce plants metabolic response, regulate the adaptive responses of plants to both, biotic and abiotic stresses. It is proven by increased JA synthesis in plants exposure to abiotic stresses under the influence of exogenous JA and its derivatives; reduced resistance to abiotic stress in plants genetically defective in JA synthesis or jasmonate signaling (Kolupaev et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Kolupaev YE, Yastreb TO, Dmitriev AP (2023) Signal mediators in the implementation of jasmonic acids protective effect on plants under abiotic stresses. Plants 12(14):2631. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/plants12142631&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3649">2023</a>). So that the application of JA in <i>Pinus sylvestirs</i> L. seedlings induced metabolic changes, while increased antioxidant enzyme activity, total phenol content and Cx+c content. It is recommended as regulator positively affecting seedlings condition. (Beniuyt et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Beniuyt E, snien I, Sirgedait-ien V, Vaitieknait D (2023) Genotype-dependent jasmonic acid effect on Pinus sylvestris L. growth and induced systemic resistance indicators. Plants 12(2):255. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/plants12020255&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3655">2023</a>). JA is associated in many plant growth and development processes, such as leaf development, root growth, blossoming and fruiting. (Bao et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Bao YJ, Chen JX, Zhang Y, Fernie AR, Zhang J, Huang BX, Zhu FY, Cao FL (2023) Emerging role of jasmonic acid in woody plant development. Authorea. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.22541/au.167420536.65415896/v1&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3658">2023</a>). At present, taking into account above-described positive effect of JA on woody plants, it is a need to expand the research in acclimatized plants.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec15">Salicylic acid</h4><p>Salicylic acid (SA) is a phenolic chemical being promising potential plant growth stimulator. It plays a significant role in the response to abiotic stresses. It has an impact on the secondary metabolism of plants (Sivanandhan et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2013" title="Sivanandhan G, Kapil Dev G, Jeyaraj M, Rajesh M, Muthuselvam M, Selvaraj N, Manickavasagam M, Ganapathi A (2013) A promising approach on biomass accumulation and with anolides production in cell suspension culture of Withania somnifera (L.) Dunal. Protoplasma 250(4):885898" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR167" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3670">2013</a>). Low concentration of SA causes interaction with stress-signaling systems and can stimulate secondary metabolite synthesis (Ghasemzadeh and Jaafar <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Ghasemzadeh A, Jaafar HZE (2011) Effect of CO2 enrichment on some primary and secondary metabolites synthesis in ginger (Zingiber officinale Roscoe). Int J Mol Sci 12(2):11011114" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3673">2011</a>; Ma et al.<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Ma X, Qian R, Zhang J, Hu Q, Qian R (2017) Salicylic Acid alleviates the adverse effects of salt stress on Dianthus superbus (Caryophyllaceae) by activating photosynthesis, protecting morphological structure, and enhancing the antioxidant system. Front Plant Sci 8:600. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3389/fpls.2017.00600&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR107" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3676">2017</a>). An increase in endogenous SA levels contributes to stomatal closure, which is preasumably caused by production of ROS, which is induced by SA. Yang et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Yang Y, Zhang R, Leng P, Hu Z, Shen M (2018) Effect of exogenous salicylic acid on the physiological and biochemical processes of Ligustrum lucidum during natural cold acclimation. Hort Sci Horts 53(6): 859864. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.21273/HORTSCI12949-18&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR182" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3679">2018</a>) suggested SA as regulator improved freezing tolerance of <i>Ligustrum lucidum</i>. Dobhal et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2023" title="Dobhal P, Agnihotri S, Ashfaqullah S, Tamta S (2023) Effect of salicylic acid elicitor on antioxidant potential and chemical composition of in vitro raised plants of Berberis asiatica Roxb. ex DC. Natural Product Res 37(18):31143121. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/14786419.2022.2141737&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3686">2023</a>) developed the propagation system of <i>Berberis asiatica</i> by application of SA which accelerated stems production and improving the antioxidant capacity of the plantlets. Medium supplemented with 25ppm SA in <i>Dimocarpus longan</i>Lour. micropropagation produced the highest percentage of antioxidative apigenin production (Ahmed et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2022" title="Ahmed MEsAE  (2022) In vitro propagation for conservation and genetic fidelity of the near threatened Dimocarpus longan plant. J Genet Eng Biotechnol 20(1):130. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1186/s43141-022-00406-4&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3695">2022</a>). In the view of above it is likely SA as a potential growth stimulant of acclimatized woody microplants.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Various substances in the acclimatization of woody plants</h3><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec17">Biostimulators</h4><p>According to the European Biostimulants Industry Council (EBIC), a biostimulant contains substances and/or microorganisms that, when applied to plants or their rhizosphere, stimulate natural plant processes to increase nutrient uptake, stress tolerance, and crop quality (du Jardin <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2015" title="du Jardin P (2015) Plant biostimulants: definition, concept, main categories and regulation. Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 196:314. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2015.09.021&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3711">2015</a>). Biostimulants can be effective in rooting ornamental trees and shrubs (Ponomarenko et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2011" title="Ponomarenko A, Qur D, Clanet CA (2011) Universal law for capillary rise in corners. J Fluid Mech 666:146154. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1017/S0022112010005276&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR139" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3714">2011</a>). Research has shown that using biostimulants during the acclimatization stage can have a positive impact on plant growth and survival (Galzy and Compan <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1992" title="Galzy R, Compan D (1992) Remarks on mixotrophic and autotrophic carbon nutrition on Vitis plantlets cultured in vitro. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 31:239244. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF00036230&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3717">1992</a>; Dimitrova et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Dimitrova N, Nacheva L, Aleksandrova D (2021) Influence of biostimulators regoplant and charkor on growth and development of micropropagated pear plants at acclimatization stage. In: Proceedings of the 5th Balkan Scientific Conference on Biology, pp 1724." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3720">2021</a>; Dimitrova and Aleksandrova <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Dimitrova N, Aleksandrova D (2021) Effect of biostimulator Regoplant on acclimatization of micropropagated GiselA 6 cherry rootstock in floating system. Sci Pap Ser B Hortic LXIV:4955." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3723">2021</a>). The beneficial effects of it have been confirmed in perennials, such as the Kelpak preparation in <i>Hosta</i> sp. (rdgh et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2019" title="rdgh M, Beregi Z, Tillyn Mndy A (2019) The effect of different biostimulators on morphological and biochemical parameters of micropropagated Hosta Gold Drop. Int J Hortic Sci 25(19). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.31421/IJHS/25/1-2./2357&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR126" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3730">2019</a>). The application of Charkor at a concentration of 0.5mL L<sup>1</sup>+IAA on glasshouse-propagated pear rootstock had a long-term positive impact on growth parameters during the acclimatization stage (Dimitrova and Berova <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Dimitrova N, Berova M (2020) Optimisation of rooting and acclimatization of Pyrus communis L. with the biostimulator Charkor. Silva Balcanica 20(3):4756" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3735">2020</a>). Similarly, using the biostimulant Regoplant on acclimatized cherry rootstock Schattenmorelle<i>Prunus canescens</i> (0.1mL L<sup>1</sup>) in a floating system resulted in the highest plant survival rates and significantly affected plant growth parameters (Dimitrova et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Dimitrova N, Nikolova V, Aleksandrova D, Nacheva L (2020) Effect of biostimulator Regoplant on acclimatization of micropropagated Gisela 6 cherry rootstock in floating system. Scientific Papers. Series b, Horticulture LXIV(2)." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3744">2020</a>). Similar results were obtained when studying <i>Pyrus communis</i> L. Old Home x Farmingdale with Charkor. The authors emphasized the simultaneous positive effects of it and the modern floating system on the success of pear rootstock acclimatization (Dimitrova et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Dimitrova N, Nacheva L, Aleksandrova D (2021) Influence of biostimulators regoplant and charkor on growth and development of micropropagated pear plants at acclimatization stage. In: Proceedings of the 5th Balkan Scientific Conference on Biology, pp 1724." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3750">2021</a>).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec18">Chitozan</h4><p>There are reports on the use of chitosan in plant acclimatization. It is an eco-friendly biopolymer derived from chitin and exhibits good biodegradability, bioactivity, and biocompatibility (Malerba and Cerana <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2018" title="Malerba M, Cerana R (2018) Recent advances of chitosan applications in plants. Polymers 10(2):118. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/polym10020118&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR110" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3761">2018</a>; Kruczek et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Kruczek A, Krupa-Makiewicz M, Ochmian I (2021) Micropropagation, rooting, and acclimatization of two cultivars of goji (Lycium chinense). Not Bot Horti Agrobot Cluj-Napoca 49(2):12271. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.15835/nbha49212271&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3764">2021</a>). Chitozan has been reported to induce various biological responses in plants, depending on its structure and concentration, species, and developmental stage. In stressful conditions, it activates numerous plant defense mechanisms (Asghari-Zakaria et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2009" title="Asghari-Zakaria R, Maleki-Zanjani B, Sedghi E (2009) Effect of in vitro chitosan application on growth and minituber yield of Solanum tuberosum L. Plant Soil Env 55(6):252256" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3767">2009</a>; Baque et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2012" title="Baque MA, Shiragi HK, Lee EJ, Paek KY (2012) Elicitor effect of chitosan and pectin on the biosynthesis of anthraquinones, phenolics and flavonoids in adventitious root suspension cultures of Morinda citrifolia (L.). Aus J Crop Sci 6(9):13491355" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3770">2012</a>; El Hadrami et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="El Hadrami A, Adam LR, El Hadrami I, Daayf F (2010) Chitosan in plant protection. Mar Drugs 8:968987. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3390/md8040968&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3773">2010</a>). Kruczek et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Kruczek A, Krupa-Makiewicz M, Ochmian I (2021) Micropropagation, rooting, and acclimatization of two cultivars of goji (Lycium chinense). Not Bot Horti Agrobot Cluj-Napoca 49(2):12271. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.15835/nbha49212271&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3777">2021</a>) point out the positive impact of chitosan on rhizogenesis and growth parameters of goji berries (<i>Lycium chinense</i>) during both in vitro and <i>ex vitro</i> rooting, which resulted in a higher success in acclimatizing these plants. Veraplakorn and Kudan, (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2021" title="Veraplakorn V, Kudan S (2021) Chitosan elicitor stimulation of in vitro growth and ex vitro acclimatization of Lantana camara L. Agric Nat Resour 55: 431439. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.34044/j.anres.2021.55.3.13&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR174" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3786">2021</a>), while studying the effect of chitosan on the acclimatization of <i>Lantana camara</i> and other factors, demonstrated the positive influence of using 1.5mg L<sup>1</sup> IBA+0.3mg L<sup>1</sup> HMC, as well as soil and foliar treatment with 0.6mg L<sup>1</sup> HMC three times a week, on the highest biomass production and achieved a plant survival rate of 82.0%.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec19">Mycorrhizal plants and rhizobacteria (PPGRs)</h4><p>Mycorrhiza is known as a mutual interaction between the roots of higher plants and fungi. Given the beneficial effects of its, young acclimatized plants require fungal colonization to enhance the growth and development of the rhizosphere. Studies have already demonstrated that mycorrhization significantly reduces the mortality of acclimatized plants and improves the production of high-quality perennial plants like bananas (Ortas et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2017" title="Ortas , Rafique M, Akpinar C, Kacar YA (2017) Growth media and mycorrhizal species effect on acclimatization and nutrient uptake of banana plantlets. Sci Hortic (Amsterdam) 217:5560. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scienta.2017.01.025&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR127" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3807">2017</a>). Inoculating acclimatized avocado plants with <i>Glomus</i> sp. fungi contributed to improved growth (in a non-sterile medium) as well as in cherry rootstocks enhanced growth and the uptake of Zn and P (Aka-Kaar et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2010" title="Aka-Kaar Y, Akpinar C, Agar A, Yalin-Mendi Y, Sere S, Orta I (2010) The effect of mycorrhiza in nutrient uptake and biomass of cherry rootstocks during acclimatization. Rom Biotechnol Lett 15(3):52465252" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3813">2010</a>). Yilmaz et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Yilmaz N, etiner S, Orta  (2020) The effects of the mycorrhiza on plant growth during the effects of the mycorrhiza on plant growth during acclimatization of some in vitro grown. Int J Agric Nat Sci 13(1):1019" href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR183" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3816">2020</a>) demonstrated that inoculating sweet cherry (<i>Prunus avium</i> L.) with <i>Funneliformis fasciculatum</i> and <i>F. mosseae</i> fungi resulted in increased uptake of Zn and P, as well as higher P content in the tissues and growth parameters. However, there was no impact on the survival rate of acclimatized plants. The colonization positively influenced photosynthesis, transpiration, stomatal conductance, and the accumulation of N, P, Ca, Cu, Zn, and Mn in the roots and leaves. Inoculated <i>Juglans regia</i> L. plants also increased the success of transfer (Dolcet-Sanjuan <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1996" title="Dobhal P, Agnihotri S, Ashfaqullah S, Tamta S (2023) Effect of salicylic acid elicitor on antioxidant potential and chemical composition of in vitro raised plants of Berberis asiatica Roxb. ex DC. Natural Product Res 37(18):31143121. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/14786419.2022.2141737&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3832">1996</a>). Multiple applications of the commercially available product, containing <i>Acremonium lichenicola</i> fungi, significantly improved plant survival rates to approximately 60% (Timofeeva et al. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2014" title="Suharyanto S, Forestry S, Rahayu W, Lopez GA (2016) Ex vitro rooting in Acacia crassicarpa micropropagation. Development and application of vegetative propagation technologies in plantation forestry to cope with changing climate and environment Proceedings of IUFRO Conference. Vol. 100." href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR169" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3838">2014</a>). Inoculation with fungi also led to a high survival rate (88%) for grapevines. Additionally, there are reports of using plant growth-promoting rhizobacteria (PGPR) for acclimatized woody plants. The application of phosphate-mobilizing and nitrogen-fixing bacteria helps promote the acclimatization of micropropagated plantlets to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions. Konstantinov et al. (<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2020" title="Konstantinov AV, Ostrikova MY, Kulagin DV (2020) Development of a scheme for acclimatization of woody plants regenerants using microbial biopesticides. In: Abstract book of the 2nd International Scientific Conference Plants and Microbes: the Future of Biotechnology Plamic 2020 (Plamic 2020 Organizing committee, 2020). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.28983/PLAMIC2020.128&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3845">2020</a>) found that the use of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> pACD, <i>Pseudomonas mendocina</i>, <i>Agrobacterium</i> sp., and <i>Pseudomonas</i> sp. 10 strains increased the survival and growth of <i>Betula</i> <i>pubescens Ehrh</i>. and <i>Populus tremula</i> L.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Concluding remarks and future prospects"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec20-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec20">Concluding remarks and future prospects</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec20-content"><p>The acclimatization process is generally challenging for in vitro cultured plants due to the lack of cellular support structures to maintain water content within the plantlet. This is mainly due to the physicochemical conditions inside the culture vessels (Kozai and Kubota <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1997" title="Kozai T, Kubota CJB (1997) Environmental control for the large-scale production of plants through in vitro techniques. Plant Cell Tissue Org Cult 51:4956. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.15835/nbha49212271&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3880">1997</a>) associated to a heterotrophic or mixotrophic growth conditions that may generate anomalies (Galzy and Compan <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1992" title="Galzy R, Compan D (1992) Remarks on mixotrophic and autotrophic carbon nutrition on Vitis plantlets cultured in vitro. Plant Cell Tissue Organ Cult 31:239244. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/BF00036230&#xA;                  &#xA;                " href="/article/10.1007/s11240-024-02923-1#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d128225355e3883">1992</a>). The morphology, anatomy, and physiology of plants regenerated in vitro do not make it easy for them to survive after being transferred to unfavorable <i>ex vitro</i> conditions, such as growth chambers, greenhouses, or later in the field. This is particularly true for woody plants. Therefore, it is essential to ensure a gradual transition of growth conditions for acclimatized plants to reduce the stress they may experience when moved to <i>ex vitro</i> conditions. Stress minimization can also be achieved through the use of pre-acclimatization or acclimatization in a controlled environment. The supplementation of plants with CO<sub>2</sub>, aimed at adapting them to autotrophy, can also be significant in acclimatizing woody plants. The use of properly formulated nutrient solutions during the propagation stage in vitro can also be crucial during the acclimatization process. To enhance the efficiency of acclimatization, various substances and preparations that positively affect plant processes and, consequently, improve the condition and survival of plants, are also used during both in vitro propagation and acclimatization stages. The beneficial impact of growth regulators, chitosan, mycorrhization and growth-promoting rhizobacteria on various woody plant species has been confirmed.</p></div></div></section>
                                </div>

              <p>Data sharing is not applicable to this article as no datasets were generated.</p>

                  </dd></dl></div></div></section><div id="MagazineFulltextArticleBodySuffix"><section aria-labelledby="Bib1" data-title="References"><div class="c-article-section" id="Bib1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Bib1">References</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Bib1-content"><div data-container-section="references"><ul class="c-article-references" data-track-component="outbound reference" data-track-context="references section"><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item"><p class="c-article-references__text" id="ref-CR1">Ahammed GJ, Li X, Liu A, Chen S (2020) Brassinosteroids in plant tolerance to abiotic stress. J Plant Growth Regul 39:14511464. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0" data-track="click_references" data-track-action="external reference" data-track-value="external reference" data-track-label="10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0">https://doi.org/10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0</a></p><p class="c-article-references__links u-hide-print"><a data-track="click_references" rel="noopener" data-track-label="10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0" data-track-item_id="10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0" data-track-value="article reference" data-track-action="article reference" href="https://link.springer.com/doi/10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0" aria-label="Article reference 1" data-doi="10.1007/s00344-020-10098-0">Article</a>

Agrofor Syst 71:195200. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1" data-track="click_references" data-track-action="external reference" data-track-value="external reference" data-track-label="10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1">https://doi.org/10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1</a></p><p class="c-article-references__links u-hide-print"><a data-track="click_references" rel="noopener" data-track-label="10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1" data-track-item_id="10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1" data-track-value="article reference" data-track-action="article reference" href="https://link.springer.com/doi/10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1" aria-label="Article reference 2" data-doi="10.1007/s10457-007-9078-1">Article</a>
